style="background:transparent;text-align:center;;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_historiography" title="Chinese historiography">Chinese historiography</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Chinese_history" title="Timeline of Chinese history">Timeline of Chinese history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dynasties_in_Chinese_history" title="Dynasties in Chinese history">Dynasties in Chinese history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Languages_of_China" title="Languages of China">Linguistic history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_art" title="Chinese art">Art history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_China" title="Economic history of China">Economic history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_education_in_China" title="History of education in China">Education history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_China" title="History of science and technology in China">Science and technology history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Legal_history_of_China" title="Legal history of China">Legal history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Media_history_of_China" title="Media history of China">Media history</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_history_of_China_(pre-1911)" title="Military history of China (pre-1911)">Military history</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Naval_history_of_China" title="Naval history of China">Naval history</a></li></ul>\n</div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="8" style="line-height: 125%; font-size: 80%; padding: 2px 2px 2px 3px; border-top: 1px solid #777; background: #FEC; text-align:center;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_China" title="Template:History of China"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_China" title="Template talk:History of China"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_China&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The earliest known written records of the <b>history of China</b> date from as early as 1250 BC, from the <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a> (c. 1600&#8211;1046 BC), during the king <a href="/wiki/Wu_Ding" title="Wu Ding">Wu Ding</a>\'s reign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-William-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> who was recorded as the twenty-first Shang king by the written records of Shang dynasty unearthed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chinaKnowledge_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-chinaKnowledge-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniIndiana_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-uniIndiana-4">[4]</a></sup> Ancient historical texts such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Records_of_the_Grand_Historian" title="Records of the Grand Historian">Records of the Grand Historian</a></i> (c. 100 BC) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Bamboo_Annals" title="Bamboo Annals">Bamboo Annals</a></i> (296 BC) describe a <a href="/wiki/Xia_dynasty" title="Xia dynasty">Xia dynasty</a> (c. 2070&#8211;1600 BC) before the Shang, but no writing is known from the period, and Shang writings do not indicate the existence of the Xia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Ancient_Dynasties_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Ancient_Dynasties-5">[5]</a></sup> The Shang ruled in the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> valley, which is commonly held to be the cradle of Chinese civilization. However, <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> civilizations originated at various cultural centers along both the Yellow River and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>. These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_river_civilization" title="Yellow river civilization">Yellow River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_civilization" title="Yangtze civilization">Yangtze civilizations</a> arose millennia before the Shang. With thousands of years of continuous history, China is one of the world\'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilizations</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and is regarded as one of the <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">cradles of civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046&#8211;256 BC) supplanted the Shang, and introduced the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_of_Heaven" title="Mandate of Heaven">Mandate of Heaven</a> to justify their rule. The central Zhou government began to weaken due to external and internal pressures in the 8th century BC, and the country eventually splintered into smaller states during the <a href="/wiki/Spring_and_Autumn_period" title="Spring and Autumn period">Spring and Autumn period</a>. These states became independent and warred with one another in the following <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a>. Much of traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" title="Culture of China">Chinese culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_literature" title="Chinese literature">literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_philosophy" title="Chinese philosophy">philosophy</a> first developed during those troubled times.\n</p><p>In 221 BC <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">Qin Shi Huang</a> <a href="/wiki/Qin%27s_wars_of_unification" title="Qin\'s wars of unification">conquered the various warring states</a> and created for himself the title of <i>Huangdi</i> or "<a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">emperor</a>" of the <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin</a>, marking the beginning of imperial China. However, the oppressive government fell soon after his death, and was supplanted by the longer-lived <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> (206 BC &#8211; 220 AD). Successive dynasties developed <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucratic</a> systems that enabled the emperor to control vast territories directly. In the 21 centuries from 206 BC until AD 1912, routine administrative tasks were handled by a special elite of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scholar-officials" title="Scholar-officials">scholar-officials</a></i>. Young men, well-versed in calligraphy, history, literature, and philosophy, were carefully selected through difficult government examinations. China\'s last dynasty was the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a> (1644&#8211;1912), which was replaced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912-1949)" title="Republic of China (1912-1949)">Republic of China</a> in 1912, and in the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a> in 1949, resulting in two <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> states claiming to be the <a href="/wiki/One-China_policy" title="One-China policy">legitimate government of all China</a>.\n</p><p>Chinese history has alternated between periods of political unity and peace, and periods of war and <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed statehood</a> &#8211; the most recent being the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> (1927&#8211;1949). China was occasionally dominated by steppe peoples, most of whom were eventually assimilated into the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> culture and population. Between eras of multiple kingdoms and warlordism, <a href="/wiki/Dynasties_in_Chinese_history" title="Dynasties in Chinese history">Chinese dynasties</a> have ruled parts or all of China; in some eras control stretched as far as <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, as at present. Traditional culture, and influences from other parts of Asia and the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> (carried by waves of immigration, <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">cultural assimilation</a>, expansion, and foreign contact), form the basis of the modern culture of China.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r872693506">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Paleolithic_.283.3_Ma_.7E_12_ka.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paleolithic_(3.3_Ma_~_12_ka)">Paleolithic (3.3 Ma ~ 12 ka)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Paleolithic_sites_in_China" title="List of Paleolithic sites in China">List of Paleolithic sites in China</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:318px;max-width:318px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2128" data-file-width="2649" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg/150px-Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg/225px-Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg/300px-Linharaptor_exquistus.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Linheraptor" title="Linheraptor">Linheraptor</a>, a genus of dromaeosaurid dinosaur which lived in what is now China in the Late Cretaceous.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tarbocosmo.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" width="160"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Tarbosaurus" title="Tarbosaurus">Tarbosaurus</a>, a genus of tyrannosaurid theropod dinosaur that lived at the end of the Late Cretaceous Period. Fossils have been recovered in the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>What is now China was inhabited by <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> more than a million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MagnetostratigraphicDating_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-MagnetostratigraphicDating-8">[8]</a></sup> Recent study shows that the stone tools found at <a href="/wiki/Xiaochangliang" title="Xiaochangliang">Xiaochangliang</a> site are <a href="/wiki/Magnetostratigraphy" title="Magnetostratigraphy">magnetostratigraphically</a> dated to 1.36 million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xiaochangliang_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Xiaochangliang-9">[9]</a></sup> The archaeological site of <a href="/wiki/Xihoudu" title="Xihoudu">Xihoudu</a> in Shanxi Province has evidence of use of fire by <i>Homo erectus</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xihoudu_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Xihoudu-10">[10]</a></sup> which is dated 1.27 million years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MagnetostratigraphicDating_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-MagnetostratigraphicDating-8">[8]</a></sup> and <i>Homo erectus</i> fossils in China include the <a href="/wiki/Yuanmou_Man" title="Yuanmou Man">Yuanmou Man</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lantian_Man" title="Lantian Man">Lantian Man</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peking_Man" title="Peking Man">Peking Man</a>. Fossilised teeth of <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> dating to 125,000&#8211;80,000 BC have been discovered in <a href="/wiki/Fuyan_Cave" title="Fuyan Cave">Fuyan Cave</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dao_County" title="Dao County">Dao County</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>  Evidence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Palaeolithic" title="Middle Palaeolithic">Middle Palaeolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Levallois_technique" title="Levallois technique">Levallois</a> technology has been found in the lithic assemblage of <a href="/wiki/Guanyindong" title="Guanyindong">Guanyindong</a> Cave site in southwest China, dated to approximately 170,000&#8211;80,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neolithic">Neolithic</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Neolithic_cultures_of_China" title="List of Neolithic cultures of China">List of Neolithic cultures of China</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_river_civilization" title="Yellow river civilization">Yellow river civilization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_civilization" title="Yangtze civilization">Yangtze civilization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liao_civilization" title="Liao civilization">Liao civilization</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Neolithic</div><div class="tsingle" class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:89px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bone_Arrowheads,_Jiahu_site.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Bone_Arrowheads%2C_Jiahu_site.jpg/225px-Bone_Arrowheads%2C_Jiahu_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Bone_Arrowheads%2C_Jiahu_site.jpg/300px-Bone_Arrowheads%2C_Jiahu_site.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Bone Arrowheads, <a href="/wiki/Peiligang_culture" title="Peiligang culture">Peiligang culture</a> (7000&#8211;5000 BC)</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:135px;max-width:135px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun(Neolithic)_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1206" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG/133px-Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG/200px-Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG/266px-Butterfly-shaped_ivory_vessel_with_the_pattern_of_two_birds_facing_the_sun%28Neolithic%29_in_Zhejiang_Museum.JPG 2x" width="133"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Butterfly-shaped ivory vessel with the pattern of two birds facing the sun, <a href="/wiki/Hemudu_culture" title="Hemudu culture">Hemudu culture</a> (5500&#8211;3300 BC)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemudu_Site_Museum,_2017-08-12_36.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4016" data-file-width="6016" decoding="async" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg/151px-Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg/227px-Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg/302px-Hemudu_Site_Museum%2C_2017-08-12_36.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Pottery artifacts from Hemudu culture (5500&#8211;3300 BC)</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> age in China can be traced back to about 10,000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neolithic_period_in_china_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-neolithic_period_in_china-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The earliest evidence of cultivated rice, found by the Yangtze River, is carbon-dated to 8,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pringle_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pringle-14">[14]</a></sup>  Early evidence for proto-Chinese <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> agriculture is <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon-dated</a> to about 7000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>  Farming gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Jiahu" title="Jiahu">Jiahu</a> culture (7000 to 5800 BC). At <a href="/wiki/Damaidi" title="Damaidi">Damaidi</a> in Ningxia, 3,172 <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_signs_in_China" title="Neolithic signs in China">cliff carvings</a> dating to 6000&#8211;5000 BC have been discovered, "featuring 8,453 individual characters such as the sun, moon, stars, gods and scenes of hunting or grazing".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Attribution_needed" title="Wikipedia:Attribution needed"><span title="This sentence may contain perspectives and opinions without stating whose they are. (January 2019)">attribution needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These pictographs are reputed to be similar to the earliest characters confirmed to be written Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Chinese <a href="/wiki/Proto-writing" title="Proto-writing">proto-writing</a> existed in Jiahu around 7000 BC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earliest_writing_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-earliest_writing-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dadiwan_culture" title="Dadiwan culture">Dadiwan</a> from 5800 BC to 5400 BC, Damaidi around 6000 BC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Banpo" title="Banpo">Banpo</a> dating from the 5th millennium BC. Some scholars have suggested that <a href="/wiki/Jiahu_symbols" title="Jiahu symbols">Jiahu symbols</a> (7th millennium BC) were the earliest Chinese writing system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earliest_writing_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-earliest_writing-17">[17]</a></sup> Excavation of a <a href="/wiki/Peiligang_culture" title="Peiligang culture">Peiligang culture</a> site in <a href="/wiki/Xinzheng" title="Xinzheng">Xinzheng</a> county, <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a>, found a community that flourished in 5,500 to 4,900 BC, with evidence of agriculture, constructed buildings, pottery, and burial of the dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> With agriculture came increased population, the ability to store and redistribute crops, and the potential to support specialist craftsmen and administrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pringle_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pringle-14">[14]</a></sup> In late Neolithic times, the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> valley began to establish itself as a center of <a href="/wiki/Yangshao_culture" title="Yangshao culture">Yangshao culture</a> (5000 BC to 3000 BC), and the first villages were founded; the most archaeologically significant of these was found at <a href="/wiki/Banpo" title="Banpo">Banpo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Later, Yangshao culture was superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Longshan_culture" title="Longshan culture">Longshan culture</a>, which was also centered on the Yellow River from about 3000 BC to 2000 BC.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">Bronze Age</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bronze_Age_sites_in_China" title="List of Bronze Age sites in China">List of Bronze Age sites in China</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Bronze Age</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:108px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1553" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg/140px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg/210px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg/280px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_jade_disk.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Jade <a href="/wiki/Bi_(jade)" title="Bi (jade)">bi</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Liangzhu_culture" title="Liangzhu culture">Liangzhu culture</a> (3400&#8211;2250 BC).</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:146px;max-width:146px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:108px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg/144px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg/216px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg/288px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_jue.jpg 2x" width="144"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Bronze <i><a href="/wiki/Jue_(vessel)" title="Jue (vessel)">jue</a></i> (wine vessel) from <a href="/wiki/Erlitou_culture" title="Erlitou culture">Erlitou culture</a> (1900&#8211;1500 BC).</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Bronze artifacts have been found at the <a href="/wiki/Majiayao_culture" title="Majiayao culture">Majiayao culture</a> site (between 3100 and 2700 BC),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Bronze Age is also represented at the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Xiajiadian_culture" title="Lower Xiajiadian culture">Lower Xiajiadian culture</a>  (2200&#8211;1600 BC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>) site in northeast China. <a href="/wiki/Sanxingdui" title="Sanxingdui">Sanxingdui</a> located in what is now <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> province is believed to be the site of a major ancient city, of a previously unknown Bronze Age culture (between 2000 and 1200 BC). The site was first discovered in 1929 and then re-discovered in 1986. Chinese archaeologists have identified the Sanxingdui culture to be part of the ancient kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Shu_(state)" title="Shu (state)">Shu</a>, linking the artifacts found at the site to its early legendary kings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p><span id="Iron_Age"></span>\n<a href="/wiki/Ferrous_metallurgy" title="Ferrous metallurgy">Ferrous metallurgy</a> begins to appear in the late 6th century in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangzi_River" title="Yangzi River">Yangzi Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Higham_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Higham-26">[26]</a></sup> \nA <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomahawk_(axe)" title="Tomahawk (axe)">tomahawk</a> with a blade of <a href="/wiki/Meteoric_iron" title="Meteoric iron">meteoric iron</a>  excavated near the city of <a href="/wiki/Gaocheng_District" title="Gaocheng District">Gaocheng</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shijiazhuang" title="Shijiazhuang">Shijiazhuang</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a> province) has been dated to the  14th century BC.\nFor this reason, authors such as Liana Chua and Mark Elliott have used the term "Iron Age" by convention for the transitional period of c. 500 BC to 100 BC, roughly corresponding to the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a> of Chinese historiography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>\nAn Iron Age culture of the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">Tibetan Plateau</a> has tentatively been associated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhang_Zhung_culture" title="Zhang Zhung culture">Zhang Zhung culture</a> described in early Tibetan writings.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_China">Ancient China</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Xia_dynasty_.282070.E2.80.931600_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Xia_dynasty_(2070&#8211;1600_BC)">Xia dynasty (2070&#8211;1600 BC)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Xia_dynasty" title="Xia dynasty">Xia dynasty</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Xia_dynasty" title="Xia dynasty">Xia dynasty</a> of China (from c. 2070 to c. 1600 BC) is the first dynasty to be described in ancient historical records such as <a href="/wiki/Sima_Qian" title="Sima Qian">Sima Qian</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Records_of_the_Grand_Historian" title="Records of the Grand Historian">Records of the Grand Historian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bamboo_Annals" title="Bamboo Annals">Bamboo Annals</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Ancient_Dynasties_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Ancient_Dynasties-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The dynasty was considered <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mythology" title="Chinese mythology">mythical</a> by historians until scientific excavations found early <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> sites at <a href="/wiki/Erlitou_culture" title="Erlitou culture">Erlitou</a>, Henan in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> With few clear records matching the Shang oracle bones, it remains unclear whether these sites are the remains of the Xia dynasty or of another culture from the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Excavations that overlap the alleged time period of the Xia indicate a type of culturally similar groupings of chiefdoms. <a href="/wiki/Proto-writing" title="Proto-writing">Early markings</a> from this period <a href="/wiki/Jiahu_symbols" title="Jiahu symbols">found on pottery and shells</a> are thought to be ancestral to modern <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Chinese characters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to ancient records, the dynasty ended around 1600 BC as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mingtiao" title="Battle of Mingtiao">Battle of Mingtiao</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Shang_dynasty_.281600.E2.80.931046_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Shang_dynasty_(1600&#8211;1046_BC)">Shang dynasty (1600&#8211;1046 BC)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Bronze_Age" title="Chinese Bronze Age">Chinese Bronze Age</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" data-file-width="1808" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG/112px-Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG/168px-Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG/224px-Dinastia_shang%2C_tipode_ding_biansato%2C_xiii-xii_sec._ac.JPG 2x" width="112"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Ding_(vessel)" title="Ding (vessel)">Ding</a>, a Shang-dynasty bronze</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:157px;max-width:157px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:139px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2564" data-file-width="2844" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg/155px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg/233px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg/310px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_bronze_battle_axe.jpg 2x" width="155"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Bronze Battle Axe, Shang dynasty (1600&#8211;1046 B.C.). Excavated at Yidu, Shangdong Province.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Archaeological findings providing evidence for the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a>, c. 1600&#8211;1046 BC, are divided into two sets. The first set, from the earlier Shang period, comes from sources at <a href="/wiki/Erligang_culture" title="Erligang culture">Erligang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhengzhou" title="Zhengzhou">Zhengzhou</a>, and Shangcheng. The second set, from the later Shang or Yin (&#27575;) period, is at <a href="/wiki/Anyang" title="Anyang">Anyang</a>, in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a>, which has been confirmed as the last of the Shang\'s nine capitals (c. 1300&#8211;1046 BC).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The findings at Anyang include the earliest written record of the Chinese so far discovered: inscriptions of divination records in ancient Chinese writing on the bones or shells of animals &#8212; the "<a href="/wiki/Oracle_bone" title="Oracle bone">oracle bones</a>", dating from around 1250 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-William-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A series of thirty-one kings reigned over the Shang dynasty. During their reign, according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Records_of_the_Grand_Historian" title="Records of the Grand Historian">Records of the Grand Historian</a></i>, the capital city was moved six times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shiji_Yinbenji_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shiji_Yinbenji-31">[31]</a></sup> The final (and most important) move was to <a href="/wiki/Yinxu" title="Yinxu">Yin</a> in 1350 BC which led to the dynasty\'s golden age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shiji_Yinbenji_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shiji_Yinbenji-31">[31]</a></sup> The term Yin dynasty has been synonymous with the Shang dynasty in history, although it has lately been used to refer specifically to the latter half of the Shang dynasty.\n</p><p>Chinese historians in later periods were accustomed to the notion of one dynasty succeeding another, but the political situation in early China was much more complicated. Hence, as some scholars of China suggest, the Xia and the Shang can refer to political entities that existed concurrently, just as the early Zhou existed at the same time as the Shang.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Although written records found at Anyang confirm the existence of the Shang dynasty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Western scholars are often hesitant to associate settlements that are contemporaneous with the Anyang settlement with the Shang dynasty. For example, archaeological findings at <a href="/wiki/Sanxingdui" title="Sanxingdui">Sanxingdui</a> suggest a technologically advanced civilization culturally unlike Anyang. The evidence is inconclusive in proving how far the Shang realm extended from Anyang. The leading hypothesis is that Anyang, ruled by the same Shang in the official history, coexisted and traded with numerous other culturally diverse settlements in the area that is now referred to as <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Zhou_dynasty_.281046.E2.80.93256_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Zhou_dynasty_(1046&#8211;256_BC)">Zhou dynasty (1046&#8211;256 BC)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_Age_China" title="Iron Age China">Iron Age China</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Zhou dynasty (1046&#8211;256 BC)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:159px;max-width:159px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="318" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png/157px-Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png/236px-Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png/314px-Zhou_dynasty_1000_BC.png 2x" width="157"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The approximate territory of the Zhou dynasty in China.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wuwangfuchaimao.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Wuwangfuchaimao.JPG/254px-Wuwangfuchaimao.JPG 2x" width="127"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Spear_of_Fuchai" title="Spear of Fuchai">Spear of Fuchai</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:131px;max-width:131px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:96px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg/129px-You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg/194px-You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg/258px-You_with_zigzag_thunder_pattern.jpg 2x" width="129"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_bronzes" title="Chinese bronzes">Bronze</a> ritual vessel (<a href="/wiki/You_(vessel)" title="You (vessel)">You</a>), Western Zhou dynasty</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:157px;max-width:157px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:96px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Periodo_primavera_e_autunno,_ascia_o_alabarca_(ge),_V_sec._ac..JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1109" data-file-width="1777" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG/155px-Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG/233px-Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG/310px-Periodo_primavera_e_autunno%2C_ascia_o_alabarca_%28ge%29%2C_V_sec._ac..JPG 2x" width="155"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Ji_(polearm)" title="Ji (polearm)">Ji</a>, a Chinese polearm combining a spear and dagger-axe, Zhou dynasty (1046&#8211;256 BC)</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The Zhou dynasty (1046 BC to approximately 256 BC) is the longest-lasting dynasty in Chinese history. By the end of the 2nd millennium BC, the Zhou dynasty began to emerge in the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> valley, overrunning the territory of the Shang. The Zhou appeared to have begun their rule under a <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">semi-feudal</a> system. The Zhou lived west of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shang" title="Shang">Shang</a>, and the Zhou leader was appointed Western Protector by the Shang. The ruler of the Zhou, <a href="/wiki/King_Wu_of_Zhou" title="King Wu of Zhou">King Wu</a>, with the assistance of his brother, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Zhou" title="Duke of Zhou">Duke of Zhou</a>, as regent, managed to defeat the Shang at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Muye" title="Battle of Muye">Battle of Muye</a>.\n</p><p>The king of Zhou at this time invoked the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_of_Heaven" title="Mandate of Heaven">Mandate of Heaven</a> to legitimize his rule, a concept that was influential for almost every succeeding dynasty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Like Shangdi, Heaven (<i>tian</i>) ruled over all the other gods, and it decided who would rule China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It was believed that a ruler lost the Mandate of Heaven when natural disasters occurred in great number, and when, more realistically, the sovereign had apparently lost his concern for the people. In response, the royal house would be overthrown, and a new house would rule, having been granted the Mandate of Heaven.\n</p><p>The Zhou initially moved their capital west to an area near modern <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Wei_River" title="Wei River">Wei River</a>, a tributary of the Yellow River, but they would preside over a series of expansions into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> valley. This would be the first of many population migrations from north to south in Chinese history.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Spring_and_Autumn_period_.28722.E2.80.93476_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_and_Autumn_period_(722&#8211;476_BC)">Spring and Autumn period (722&#8211;476 BC)</span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_China&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Hegemons during the Spring and Autumn period of Zhou dynasty</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage" Museum</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:136px;max-width:136px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sun_Gao_Bianzhong,_picture4.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Sun_Gao_Bianzhong%2C_picture4.jpg/201px-Sun_Gao_Bianzhong%2C_picture4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Sun_Gao_Bianzhong%2C_picture4.jpg/268px-Sun_Gao_Bianzhong%2C_picture4.jpg 2x" width="134"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The Sun Gao Bianzhong, Spring and Autumn period (770&#8211;476 B.C.), excavated in 1978 from a tomb in Yingchuan, Henan.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<dl><dd><i>Capitals: <a href="/wiki/Several" title="Several">several</a> (multiple states)</i></dd></dl>\n<p>In the 8th century BC, power became decentralized during the <a href="/wiki/Spring_and_Autumn_period" title="Spring and Autumn period">Spring and Autumn period</a>, named after the influential <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_and_Autumn_Annals" title="Spring and Autumn Annals">Spring and Autumn Annals</a></i>. In this period, local military leaders used by the Zhou began to assert their power and vie for <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a>. The situation was aggravated by the invasion of other peoples from the northwest, such as the <a href="/wiki/Qin_(state)" title="Qin (state)">Qin</a>, forcing the Zhou to move their capital east to <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a>. This marks the second major phase of the Zhou dynasty: the Eastern Zhou. The Spring and Autumn period is marked by a falling apart of the central Zhou power. In each of the hundreds of states that eventually arose, local strongmen held most of the political power and continued their subservience to the Zhou kings in name only. Some local leaders even started using royal titles for themselves. China now consisted of hundreds of states, some of them only as large as a village with a fort.\n</p><p>As the era continued, larger and more powerful states annexed or claimed suzerainty over smaller ones. By the 6th century BC most small states had disappeared by being annexed and just a few large and powerful principalities dominated China. Some southern states, such as Chu and Wu, claimed independence from the Zhou, who undertook wars against some of them (Wu and Yue). Many new cities were established in this period and Chinese culture was slowly shaped.\n</p><p>Once all these powerful rulers had firmly established themselves within their respective dominions, the bloodshed focused more fully on interstate conflict in the Warring States period, which began when the three remaining &#233;lite families in the Jin state &#8211; Zhao, Wei and Han &#8211; partitioned the state. Many famous individuals such as <a href="/wiki/Laozi" title="Laozi">Laozi</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Confucius" title="Confucius">Confucius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sun_Tzu" title="Sun Tzu">Sun Tzu</a> lived during this chaotic period.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Schools_of_Thought" title="Hundred Schools of Thought">Hundred Schools of Thought</a> of Chinese philosophy blossomed during this period, and such influential intellectual movements as <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legalism_(Chinese_philosophy)" title="Legalism (Chinese philosophy)">Legalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohism" title="Mohism">Mohism</a> were founded, partly in response to the changing political world. The first two philosophical thoughts would have an enormous influence on Chinese culture.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Warring_States_period_.28476.E2.80.93221_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Warring_States_period_(476&#8211;221_BC)">Warring States period (476&#8211;221 BC)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Warring States period (476&#8211;221 BC)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:123px;max-width:123px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:122px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Streitende-Reiche2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="886" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Streitende-Reiche2.jpg/121px-Streitende-Reiche2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Streitende-Reiche2.jpg/182px-Streitende-Reiche2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Streitende-Reiche2.jpg/242px-Streitende-Reiche2.jpg 2x" width="121"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Map of the Warring States. Qin is shown in pink</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:165px;max-width:165px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:122px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji,_Warring_States_period,_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg/163px-Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg/245px-Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg/326px-Bronze_halberd_-_Duo_Ge_Tong_Ji%2C_Warring_States_period%2C_Henan_Institute_of_Historic_Relic_Archaeology_and_Research.jpg 2x" width="163"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Bronze halberd - Duo Ge Tong Ji, Warring States period (457-221 BC), excavated in 1994 in Henan.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:184px;max-width:184px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:136px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg/182px-Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg/273px-Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg/364px-Bi_with_two_dragons_and_grain_pattern.jpg 2x" width="182"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Bi disc with a dual dragon motif, <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:104px;max-width:104px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:136px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crystal_Cup(Warring_States_Period)_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG/102px-Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG/153px-Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG/204px-Crystal_Cup%28Warring_States_Period%29_in_Hangzhou_Museum.JPG 2x" width="102"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">A cup carved from <a href="/wiki/Crystal" title="Crystal">crystal</a>, unearthed at Banshan, <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>After further political consolidation, seven prominent states remained by the end of the 5th century BC, and the years in which these few states battled each other are known as the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a>. Though there remained a nominal <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou</a> king until 256 BC, he was largely a figurehead and held little real power.\n</p><p>Numerous developments were made during this period in culture and mathematics.  Examples include an important literary achievement, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zuo_Commentary" title="Zuo Commentary">Zuo Commentary</a></i> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_and_Autumn_Annals" title="Spring and Autumn Annals">Spring and Autumn Annals</a></i>, which summarizes the preceding Spring and Autumn period, and the bundle of 21 bamboo slips from the <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_Bamboo_Slips" title="Tsinghua Bamboo Slips">Tsinghua</a> collection, which was invented during this period dated to 305<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span> BC, are the worlds\' earliest example of a two digit <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_Bamboo_Slips#Decimal_multiplication_table" title="Tsinghua Bamboo Slips">decimal multiplication table</a>, indicating that sophisticated commercial arithmetic was already established during this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As neighboring territories of these warring states, including areas of modern <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Liaoning</a>, were annexed, they were governed under the new local administrative system of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commandery_(China)" title="Commandery (China)">commandery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prefecture" title="Prefecture">prefecture</a>. This system had been in use since the Spring and Autumn period, and parts can still be seen in the modern system of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Administrative divisions of the People\'s Republic of China">Sheng and Xian</a> (province and county).\n</p><p>The final expansion in this period began during the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ying_Zheng" title="Ying Zheng">Ying Zheng</a>, the king of Qin. His unification of the other six powers, and further annexations in the modern regions of <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a>, Fujian, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a> in 214 BC, enabled him to proclaim himself the <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">First Emperor</a> (Qin Shi Huang).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_China">Imperial China</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Empire of China" redirects here. For the empire founded by Yuan Shikai, see <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_China_(1915%E2%80%931916)" title="Empire of China (1915&#8211;1916)">Empire of China (1915&#8211;1916)</a>.</div>\n<p>The Imperial China Period can be divided into three subperiods: Early, Middle, and Late.\n</p><p>Major events in the Early subperiod include the Qin unification of China and their replacement by the Han, the First Split followed by the Jin unification, and the loss of north China. The Middle subperiod was marked by the Sui unification and their supplementation by the Tang, the Second Split, and the Song unification. The Late subperiod included the Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Qin_dynasty_.28221.E2.80.93207_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Qin_dynasty_(221&#8211;207_BC)">Qin dynasty (221&#8211;207 BC)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin dynasty</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Qin dynasty (221&#8211;207 BC)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:125px;max-width:125px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:120px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qin_empire_210_BCE.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="545" data-file-width="555" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Qin_empire_210_BCE.jpg/123px-Qin_empire_210_BCE.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Qin_empire_210_BCE.jpg/246px-Qin_empire_210_BCE.jpg 2x" width="123"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The territory of Qin dynasty, 210 BC</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:163px;max-width:163px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:120px;overflow:hidden"><a //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Terracotta_Army-China2.jpg/322px-Terracotta_Army-China2.jpg 2x" width="161"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The <a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">Terracotta Army</a> of <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">Qin Shi Huang</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:94px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1366" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG/142px-%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG/213px-%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG/284px-%E5%9B%9B%E5%B7%9D%E9%83%BD%E6%B1%9F%E5%A0%B01.JPG 2x" width="142"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Dujiangyan" title="Dujiangyan">Dujiangyan</a>, an irrigation project completed in 256 BC during the Warring States period of China by the State of Qin</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:94px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="1936" decoding="async" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg/142px-Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg/213px-Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg/284px-Great_wall_of_qi_2008_07_14.jpg 2x" width="142"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Ruins of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_Qi" title="Great Wall of Qi">Great Wall of Qi</a> on Dafeng Mountain in the <a href="/wiki/Changqing_District" title="Changqing District">Changqing District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">Jinan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a> province, dated back to the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Historians often refer to the period from the Qin dynasty to the end of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> as Imperial China. Though the unified reign of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang_Di" title="Qin Shi Huang Di">First Qin Emperor</a> lasted only 12 years, he managed to subdue great parts of what constitutes the core of the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> homeland and to unite them under a tightly centralized <a href="/wiki/Legalism_(Chinese_philosophy)" title="Legalism (Chinese philosophy)">Legalist</a> government seated at <a href="/wiki/Xianyang" title="Xianyang">Xianyang</a> (close to modern <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>). The doctrine of Legalism that guided the Qin emphasized strict adherence to a legal code and the absolute power of the emperor. This philosophy, while effective for expanding the empire in a military fashion, proved unworkable for governing it in peacetime. The Qin Emperor presided over the brutal silencing of political opposition, including the event known as the <a href="/wiki/Burning_of_books_and_burying_of_scholars" title="Burning of books and burying of scholars">burning of books and burying of scholars</a>. This would be the impetus behind the later Han synthesis incorporating the more moderate schools of political governance.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;max-width:277px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:143px;max-width:143px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2424" data-file-width="1984" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg/141px-Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg/212px-Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg/282px-Terrakotta_general_2010.jpg 2x" width="141"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:130px;max-width:130px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3504" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg/128px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg/192px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg/256px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n-13.jpg 2x" width="128"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">Terracotta Army</a> General (Left), Mid-rank officer of the Terracotta Army in <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a> (Right)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2573" data-file-width="2698" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg/150px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg/225px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg/300px-CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CMOC_Treasures_of_Ancient_China_exhibit_-_stone_slab_with_twelve_small_seal_characters.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stone slab with twelve Qin <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seal_characters" title="Seal characters">seal characters</a> (221&#8211;206 B.C.)</div></div></div>\n<p>Major contributions of the Qin include the concept of a centralized government, and the unification and development of the legal code, the written language, measurement, and currency of China after the tribulations of the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods. Even something as basic as the length of axles for carts&#8212;which need to match ruts in the roads&#8212;had to be made uniform to ensure a viable trading system throughout the empire. Also as part of its centralization, the Qin connected the northern border walls of the states it defeated, making the first <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a>.\n</p><p>The tribes of the north, collectively called the <a href="/wiki/Five_Barbarians" title="Five Barbarians">Wu Hu</a> by the Qin, were free from Chinese rule during the majority of the dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lewis129_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-lewis129-35">[35]</a></sup> Prohibited from trading with Qin dynasty peasants, the <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> tribe living in the <a href="/wiki/Ordos_Desert" title="Ordos Desert">Ordos</a> region in northwest China often raided them instead, prompting the Qin to retaliate. After a <a href="/wiki/Qin%27s_campaign_against_the_Xiongnu" title="Qin\'s campaign against the Xiongnu">military campaign led by General Meng Tian</a>, the region was conquered in 215 BC and agriculture was established; the peasants, however, were discontented and later revolted. The succeeding Han dynasty also expanded into the Ordos due to overpopulation, but depleted their resources in the process. Indeed, this was true of the dynasty\'s borders in multiple directions; modern <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, and regions to the southeast were foreign to the Qin, and even areas over which they had military control were culturally distinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A major Qin innovation<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> that lasted until 1912 was reliance upon a trained intellectual elite, the <i><a href="/wiki/Scholar-official" title="Scholar-official">scholar-official</a></i> ("scholar-gentlemen"). They were civil servants appointed by the Emperor to handle daily governance. Talented young men were selected through an elaborate process of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_examination" title="Imperial examination">imperial examination</a>. They had to demonstrate skill at <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a>, and had to know Confucian philosophy. Historian Wing-Tsit Chan concludes that:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Generally speaking, the record of these scholar-gentlemen has been a worthy one. It was good enough to be praised and imitated in 18th century Europe. Nevertheless, it has given China a tremendous handicap in their transition from government by men to government by law, and personal considerations in Chinese government have been a curse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p>After Emperor Qin Shi Huang\'s unnatural death due to the consumption of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a> pills,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wright_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-wright-38">[38]</a></sup> the Qin government drastically deteriorated and eventually capitulated in 207 BC after the Qin capital was captured and sacked by rebels, which would ultimately lead to the establishment of a new dynasty of a unified China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Despite the short 15-year duration of the Qin dynasty, it was immensely influential on China and the structure of future Chinese dynasties.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Han_dynasty_.28202_BC_.E2.80.93_AD_220.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Han_dynasty_(202_BC_&#8211;_AD_220)">Han dynasty (202 BC &#8211; AD 220)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Han_dynasty" title="History of the Han dynasty">History of the Han dynasty</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Han dynasty (202 BC &#8211; AD 220)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:141px;max-width:141px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:96px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Han_Dynasty_map_2CE.png"><img Road</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:123px;max-width:123px"><div class="thumbimage" title="Nanyue">Nanyue</a> in southern China</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:165px;max-width:165px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:116px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dahuting_mural,_Eastern_Han_Dynasty.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="342" data-file-width="480" decoding="async"
