srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dahuting_mural%2C_Eastern_Han_Dynasty.jpg/245px-Dahuting_mural%2C_Eastern_Han_Dynasty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dahuting_mural%2C_Eastern_Han_Dynasty.jpg/326px-Dahuting_mural%2C_Eastern_Han_Dynasty.jpg 2x" width="163"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">A mural showing women dressed in traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Hanfu" title="Hanfu">Hanfu</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> robes, <a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Dahuting_Tomb_murals" title="c:Category:Dahuting Tomb murals">from the Dahuting Tomb</a> of the late <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Han_dynasty" title="Eastern Han dynasty">Eastern Han dynasty</a> (25&#8211;220 AD), located in <a href="/wiki/Zhengzhou" title="Zhengzhou">Zhengzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> province, China</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Han">Western Han</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Han_Expansion.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="902" data-file-width="1275" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Han_Expansion.png/220px-Han_Expansion.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Han_Expansion.png/330px-Han_Expansion.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Han_Expansion.png/440px-Han_Expansion.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Han_Expansion.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the expansion of Han dynasty in the 2nd century BC</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Gaozu_of_Han" title="Emperor Gaozu of Han">Liu Bang</a>, who emerged victorious in the <a href="/wiki/Chu%E2%80%93Han_Contention" title="Chu&#8211;Han Contention">Chu&#8211;Han Contention</a> that followed the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin dynasty</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Pax_Sinica" title="Pax Sinica">golden age</a> in Chinese history, the Han dynasty\'s long period of stability and prosperity consolidated the foundation of China as a unified state under a central imperial bureaucracy, which was to last intermittently for most of the next two millennia. During the Han dynasty, territory of China was extended to most of the <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> and to areas far west. <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> was officially elevated to orthodox status and was to shape the subsequent Chinese civilization. Art, culture and science all advanced to unprecedented heights. With the profound and lasting impacts of this period of Chinese history, the dynasty name "Han" had been taken as the name of the Chinese people, now the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">dominant ethnic group</a> in modern China, and had been commonly used to refer to Chinese language and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">written characters</a>. The Han dynasty also saw many mathematical innovations being invented such as the method of <a href="/wiki/Gaussian_elimination" title="Gaussian elimination">Gaussian elimination</a> which appeared in the Chinese mathematical text <a href="/wiki/Rod_calculus#System_of_linear_equations" title="Rod calculus">Chapter Eight <i>Rectangular Arrays</i></a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nine_Chapters_on_the_Mathematical_Art" title="The Nine Chapters on the Mathematical Art">The Nine Chapters on the Mathematical Art</a></i>. Its use is illustrated in eighteen problems, with two to five equations. The first reference to the book by this title is dated to 179 AD, but parts of it were written as early as approximately 150 BC, more than 1500 years before the Europeans came up with the method in the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-princeton_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huang-Lao" title="Huang-Lao">initial laissez-faire policies</a> of Emperors <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wen_of_Han" title="Emperor Wen of Han">Wen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jing_of_Han" title="Emperor Jing of Han">Jing</a>, the ambitious <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Han" title="Emperor Wu of Han">Emperor Wu</a> brought the empire to its zenith. To consolidate his power, Confucianism, which emphasizes stability and order in a well-structured society, was given exclusive patronage to be the guiding philosophical thoughts and moral principles of the empire. <a href="/wiki/Taixue" title="Taixue">Imperial Universities</a> were established to support its study and further development, while other <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Schools_of_Thought" title="Hundred Schools of Thought">schools of thought</a> were discouraged.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:258px;max-width:258px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:China_qing_blue.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3424" data-file-width="2376" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/China_qing_blue.JPG/130px-China_qing_blue.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/China_qing_blue.JPG/195px-China_qing_blue.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/China_qing_blue.JPG/260px-China_qing_blue.JPG 2x" width="130"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs,_Western_Han.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1062" data-file-width="683" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg/120px-Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg/180px-Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg/240px-Bronze_mirror_with_painted_designs%2C_Western_Han.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><b>Left image</b>: Western-Han painted ceramic jar decorated with raised <a href="/wiki/Relief" title="Relief">reliefs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_dragon" title="Chinese dragon">dragons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fenghuang" title="Fenghuang">phoenixes</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Taotie" title="Taotie">taotie</a></i><br/> <b>Right image</b>: Reverse side of a Western-Han <a href="/wiki/TLV_mirror" title="TLV mirror">bronze mirror</a> with painted designs of a flower motif</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Han%E2%80%93Xiongnu_War" title="Han&#8211;Xiongnu War">Major military campaigns</a> were launched to weaken the nomadic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xiongnu_Empire" title="Xiongnu Empire">Xiongnu Empire</a>, limiting their influence north of the Great Wall. Along with the diplomatic efforts led by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Qian" title="Zhang Qian">Zhang Qian</a>, the sphere of influence of the Han Empire extended to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Regions" title="Western Regions">states in the Tarim Basin</a>, opened up the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> that connected China to the west, stimulating bilateral trade and cultural exchange. To the south, various small kingdoms far beyond the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> Valley were formally incorporated into the empire.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="416" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg/150px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg/225px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg/300px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg/150px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg/225px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg/300px-Warring_States_or_Western_Han_crossbow2.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">A Chinese <a href="/wiki/Crossbow" title="Crossbow">crossbow</a> mechanism with a buttplate from either the late Warring States Period or the early Han dynasty; made of bronze and inlaid with silver</div></div></div>\n<p>Emperor Wu also dispatched a <a href="/wiki/Southward_expansion_of_the_Han_dynasty" title="Southward expansion of the Han dynasty">series of military campaigns</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Baiyue" title="Baiyue">Baiyue</a> tribes. The Han annexed <a href="/wiki/Han_campaigns_against_Minyue" title="Han campaigns against Minyue">Minyue in 135 BC</a> and 111 BC, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han%E2%80%93Nanyue_War" title="Han&#8211;Nanyue War">Nanyue in 111 BC</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_campaign_against_Dian" title="Han campaign against Dian">Dian in 109 BC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Migration and military expeditions led to the cultural assimilation of the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> It also brought the Han into contact with kingdoms in Southeast Asia, introducing diplomacy and trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Han" title="Emperor Wu of Han">Emperor Wu</a>, the empire slipped into gradual stagnation and decline. Economically, the state treasury was strained by excessive campaigns and projects, while land acquisitions by elite families gradually drained the tax base. Various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consort_clan" title="Consort clan">consort clans</a> exerted increasing control over strings of incompetent emperors and eventually the dynasty was briefly interrupted by the usurpation of <a href="/wiki/Wang_Mang" title="Wang Mang">Wang Mang</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Xin_dynasty">Xin dynasty</span></h4>\n<p>In AD 9, the usurper <a href="/wiki/Wang_Mang" title="Wang Mang">Wang Mang</a> claimed that the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_of_Heaven" title="Mandate of Heaven">Mandate of Heaven</a> called for the end of the Han dynasty and the rise of his own, and he founded the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Xin_dynasty" title="Xin dynasty">Xin ("New") dynasty</a>. Wang Mang started an extensive program of land and other economic reforms, including the outlawing of slavery and land nationalization and redistribution. These programs, however, were never supported by the landholding families, because they favored the <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasants</a>. The instability of power brought about chaos, uprisings, and loss of territories. This was compounded by mass flooding of the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a>; silt buildup caused it to split into two channels and displaced large numbers of farmers. Wang Mang was eventually killed in <a href="/wiki/Weiyang_Palace" title="Weiyang Palace">Weiyang Palace</a> by an enraged peasant mob in AD 23.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Han">Eastern Han</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2566" data-file-width="4424" decoding="async" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg/170px-%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg/255px-%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg/340px-%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%9C%E6%B1%89%E9%93%9C%E5%8D%A1%E5%B0%BA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A bronze caliper from the Eastern Han period</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Emperor_Guangwu_of_Han" title="Emperor Guangwu of Han">Emperor Guangwu</a> reinstated the Han dynasty with the support of landholding and merchant families at <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a>, <i>east</i> of the former capital <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>. Thus, this new era is termed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Han_dynasty" title="Eastern Han dynasty">Eastern Han dynasty</a>. With the capable administrations of Emperors <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Ming_of_Han" title="Emperor Ming of Han">Ming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Zhang_of_Han" title="Emperor Zhang of Han">Zhang</a>, former glories of the dynasty was reclaimed, with brilliant military and cultural achievements. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xiongnu_Empire" title="Xiongnu Empire">Xiongnu Empire</a> was <a href="/wiki/Han%E2%80%93Xiongnu_War#Final_stages" title="Han&#8211;Xiongnu War">decisively defeated</a>. The diplomat and general <a href="/wiki/Ban_Chao" title="Ban Chao">Ban Chao</a> further expanded the conquests across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pamirs" title="Pamirs">Pamirs</a> to the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> thus reopening the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, and bringing trade, foreign cultures, along with the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Buddhism#Traditional_accounts" title="Chinese Buddhism">arrival of Buddhism</a>. With extensive connections with the west, the first of several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romano-Chinese_relations" title="Romano-Chinese relations">Roman embassies to China</a> were recorded in Chinese sources, coming from the sea route in AD 166, and a second one in AD 284.\n</p><p>The Eastern Han dynasty was one of the <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_of_the_Han_dynasty" title="Science and technology of the Han dynasty">most prolific era of science and technology</a> in ancient China, notably the historic invention of <a href="/wiki/Papermaking" title="Papermaking">papermaking</a> by <a href="/wiki/Cai_Lun" title="Cai Lun">Cai Lun</a>, and the numerous scientific and mathematical contributions by the famous <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Heng" title="Zhang Heng">Zhang Heng</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Three_Kingdoms_.28AD_220.E2.80.93280.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_Kingdoms_(AD_220&#8211;280)">Three Kingdoms (AD 220&#8211;280)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms" title="Three Kingdoms">Three Kingdoms</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Three Kingdoms (AD 220&#8211;280)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:117px;max-width:117px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:112px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:China_5.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/China_5.jpg/115px-China_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/China_5.jpg/173px-China_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/China_5.jpg/230px-China_5.jpg 2x" width="115"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Three Kingdoms in 262, on the eve of the conquest of Shu, Wei, and Wu.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:171px;max-width:171px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:112px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco,_Luoyang.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg/169px-Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg/254px-Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg/338px-Cao_Wei_Dynasty_fresco%2C_Luoyang.jpg 2x" width="169"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Fresco of a tomb in <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a> dated to the <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Cao Wei</a> period (220&#8211;266 AD), showing seated men wearing <i><a href="/wiki/Hanfu" title="Hanfu">Hanfu</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> robes</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>By the 2nd century, the empire declined amidst land acquisitions, invasions, and feuding between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consort_clan" title="Consort clan">consort clans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eunuch#China" title="Eunuch">eunuchs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Turban_Rebellion" title="Yellow Turban Rebellion">Yellow Turban Rebellion</a> broke out in AD 184, ushering in an era of <a href="/wiki/Warlord" title="Warlord">warlords</a>. In the ensuing turmoil, three states tried to gain predominance in the period of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms" title="Three Kingdoms">Three Kingdoms</a>. This time period has been greatly romanticized in works such as <i><a href="/wiki/Romance_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" title="Romance of the Three Kingdoms">Romance of the Three Kingdoms</a></i>.\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Cao_Cao" title="Cao Cao">Cao Cao</a> reunified the north in 208, his son proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Wei</a> dynasty in 220. Soon, Wei\'s rivals <a href="/wiki/Shu_Han" title="Shu Han">Shu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Wu" title="Eastern Wu">Wu</a> proclaimed their independence, leading China into the Three Kingdoms period. This period was characterized by a gradual decentralization of the state that had existed during the Qin and Han dynasties, and an increase in the power of great families.\n</p><p>In 266, the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Jin dynasty</a> overthrew the Wei and later unified the country in 280, but this union was short-lived.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Jin_dynasty_.28AD_266.E2.80.93420.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jin_dynasty_(AD_266&#8211;420)">Jin dynasty (AD 266&#8211;420)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">Sixteen Kingdoms</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Jin dynasty (AD 266&#8211;420)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:167px;max-width:167px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:158px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="537" data-file-width="556" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png/165px-Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png/248px-Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png/330px-Western_Jeun_Dynasty_280_CE.png 2x" width="165"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Jin_Dynasty" title="Western Jin Dynasty">Western Jin Dynasty</a>, c. 280 AD</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:121px;max-width:121px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:158px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_11.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="4592" data-file-width="3448" decoding="async" height="158" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_11.JPG/179px-2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_11.JPG/238px-2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_11.JPG 2x" width="119"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">View of Maijishan hill caves, grottoes and stairways.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:173px;max-width:173px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:128px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3448" data-file-width="4592" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG/171px-2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG/257px-2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG/342px-2016-12-15_Maijishan_Grotten_%E9%BA%A5%E7%A9%8D%E5%B1%B1%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_anagoria_14.JPG 2x" width="171"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Maijishan hill caves</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:115px;max-width:115px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:128px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P-leshenfu.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1822" data-file-width="1609" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/P-leshenfu.jpg/113px-P-leshenfu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/P-leshenfu.jpg/170px-P-leshenfu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/P-leshenfu.jpg/226px-P-leshenfu.jpg 2x" width="113"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">"The Painting of Goddess Luo Rhapsody"(in a part), Gu Kaizhi, Jin Dynasty</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The Jin dynasty was severely weakened by <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Eight_Princes" title="War of the Eight Princes">internecine fighting among imperial princes</a> and lost control of northern China after <a href="/wiki/Five_Barbarians" title="Five Barbarians">non-Han Chinese settlers</a> <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_the_Five_Barbarians" title="Uprising of the Five Barbarians">rebelled</a> and captured Luoyang and Chang\'an.  In 317, a <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Yuan_of_Jin" title="Emperor Yuan of Jin">Jin prince</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> became emperor and continued the dynasty, now known as the Eastern Jin, which held southern China for another century. Prior to this move, historians refer to the Jin dynasty as the Western Jin.\n</p><p>Northern China fragmented into a series of <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">independent kingdoms</a>, most of which were founded by <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xianbei" title="Xianbei">Xianbei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jie_people" title="Jie people">Jie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Di_(Five_Barbarians)" title="Di (Five Barbarians)">Di</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qiang_(historical_people)" title="Qiang (historical people)">Qiang</a> rulers.  These non-Han peoples were ancestors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkic_people" title="Turkic people">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetans" title="Tibetans">Tibetans</a>. Many had, to some extent, been "<a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicized</a>" long before their ascent to power. In fact, some of them, notably the <a href="/wiki/Qiang_people" title="Qiang people">Qiang</a> and the Xiongnu, had already been allowed to live in the frontier regions within the Great Wall since late Han times.  During the period of the <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">Sixteen Kingdoms</a>, warfare ravaged the north and prompted large-scale Han Chinese migration south to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze</a> Basin and Delta.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Northern_and_Southern_dynasties_.28AD_420.E2.80.93589.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_and_Southern_dynasties_(AD_420&#8211;589)">Northern and Southern dynasties (AD 420&#8211;589)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Northern_and_Southern_dynasties" title="Northern and Southern dynasties">Northern and Southern dynasties</a></div>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_China&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Northern and Southern dynasties (AD 420&#8211;589)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Southern_and_Northern_Dynasties_440_CE.png/248px-Southern_and_Northern_Dynasties_440_CE.png 2x" width="124"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Southern and Northern Dynasties, 440 AD</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage" class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanging_Monastery" title="Hanging Monastery">Hanging Monastery</a>, a temple with the combination of <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yungang5_2010.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yungang5_2010.JPG/151px-Yungang5_2010.JPG" href="/wiki/Yungang_Grottoes" title="Yungang Grottoes">Yungang Grottoes</a>, an ancient Chinese Buddhist temple grottoes near the city of Datong in the province of <a href="/wiki/Shanxi" title="Shanxi">Shanxi</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:135px;max-width:135px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jiucenglou_of_Mogao_Caves.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Jiucenglou_of_Mogao_Caves.jpg/200px-Jiucenglou_of_Mogao_Caves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Jiucenglou_of_Mogao_Caves.jpg/266px-Jiucenglou_of_Mogao_Caves.jpg 2x" width="133"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Mogao_Caves" title="Mogao Caves">Mogao Caves</a>, also known as the Thousand Buddha Grottoes, located at a religious and cultural crossroads on the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gansu_province" title="Gansu province">Gansu province</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>In the early 5th century, China entered a period known as the Northern and Southern dynasties, in which parallel regimes ruled the northern and southern halves of the country.  In the south, the Eastern Jin gave way to the <a href="/wiki/Liu_Song_dynasty" title="Liu Song dynasty">Liu Song</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Qi" title="Southern Qi">Southern Qi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liang_dynasty" title="Liang dynasty">Liang</a> and finally <a href="/wiki/Chen_dynasty" title="Chen dynasty">Chen</a>. Each of these Southern dynasties were led by Han Chinese ruling families and used <a href="/wiki/Jiankang" title="Jiankang">Jiankang</a> (modern Nanjing) as the capital. They held off attacks from the north and preserved many aspects of Chinese civilization, while northern barbarian regimes began to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinify" title="Sinify">sinify</a>.\n</p><p>In the north, the last of the Sixteen Kingdoms was extinguished in 439 by the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Wei" title="Northern Wei">Northern Wei</a>, a kingdom founded by the <a href="/wiki/Xianbei" title="Xianbei">Xianbei</a>, a nomadic people who unified northern China. The Northern Wei eventually split into the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Wei" title="Eastern Wei">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Wei" title="Western Wei">Western Wei</a>, which then became the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Qi" title="Northern Qi">Northern Qi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Zhou" title="Northern Zhou">Northern Zhou</a>. These regimes were dominated by Xianbei or Han Chinese who had married into Xianbei families. During this period most Xianbei people adopted Han surnames, eventually leading to complete assimilation into the Han.\n</p><p>Despite the division of the country, Buddhism spread throughout the land. In southern China, fierce debates about whether <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> should be allowed were held frequently by the royal court and nobles. By the end of the era, Buddhists and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoist" title="Taoist">Taoists</a> had become much more tolerant of each other.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Sui_dynasty_.28581.E2.80.93618.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sui_dynasty_(581&#8211;618)">Sui dynasty (581&#8211;618)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Sui dynasty (581&#8211;618)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cheui_Dynasty_581_CE.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="537" data-file-width="556" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Cheui_Dynasty_581_CE.png/124px-Cheui_Dynasty_581_CE.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/1400%E5%B9%B4%E5%8E%86%E5%8F%B2%E7%9A%84%E8%B5%B5%E5%B7%9E%E6%A1%A5_zhao_zhou_qiao_-_panoramio.jpg/320px-1400%E5%B9%B4%E5%8E%86%E5%8F%B2%E7%9A%84%E8%B5%B5%E5%B7%9E%E6%A1%A5_zhao_zhou_qiao_-_panoramio.jpg segmental arch bridge of stone construction.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG/192px-Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG/288px-Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG/384px-Tianlongshan_Grotto_-_Manshan_Pavillion%2C_Taiyuan%2C_Shanxi.JPG 2x" width="192"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Manshan Pavilion of the <a href="/wiki/Tianlongshan_Grottoes" title="Tianlongshan Grottoes">Tianlongshan Grottoes</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:94px;max-width:94px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:144px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1272" data-file-width="812" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg/92px-Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg/138px-Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg/184px-Sui_Yangdi_Tang.jpg 2x" width="92"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Yang Guang depicted as Emperor of Sui</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The short-lived <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a> was a pivotal period in Chinese history. Founded by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wen_of_Sui" title="Emperor Wen of Sui">Emperor Wen</a> in 581 in succession of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Zhou" title="Northern Zhou">Northern Zhou</a>, the Sui went on to conquer the <a href="/wiki/Chen_dynasty" title="Chen dynasty">Southern Chen</a> in 589 to reunify China, ending three centuries of political division. The Sui pioneered many new institutions, including the government system of <a href="/wiki/Three_Departments_and_Six_Ministries" title="Three Departments and Six Ministries">Three Departments and Six Ministries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_examination" title="Imperial examination">imperial examinations</a> for selecting officials from commoners, while improved on the systems of <a href="/wiki/Fubing_system" title="Fubing system">fubing system</a> of the army conscription and the <a href="/wiki/Equal-field_system" title="Equal-field system">Equal-field system</a> of land distributions. These policies, which were adopted by later dynasties, brought enormous population growth, and amassed excessive wealth to the state. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Chinese_coinage" title="Ancient Chinese coinage">Standardized coinage</a> were enforced throughout the unified empire. Buddhism took root as a prominent religion and was supported officially. Sui China was known for its numerous mega-construction projects. Intended for grains shipment and transporting troops, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a> was constructed, linking the capitals <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Daxing (Chang\'an)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a> to the wealthy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_China" title="Southeastern China">southeast region</a>, and in another route, to the northeast border. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall</a> was also expanded, while series of military conquests and diplomatic maneuvers further pacified its borders. However, the massive invasions of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Goguryeo%E2%80%93Sui_War" title="Goguryeo&#8211;Sui War">Goguryeo&#8211;Sui War</a> failed disastrously, triggering widespread revolts that led to <a href="/wiki/Transition_from_Sui_to_Tang" title="Transition from Sui to Tang">the fall of the dynasty</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Tang_dynasty_.28AD_618.E2.80.93907.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tang_dynasty_(AD_618&#8211;907)">Tang dynasty (AD 618&#8211;907)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Tang dynasty (AD 618&#8211;907)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:115px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tang_China_669AD.jpg"><img alt="" Dynasty in 669 AD</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:156px;max-width:156px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:115px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%E6%B2%B3%E5%8D%97_%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3_%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_-_panoramio.jpg/231px-%E6%B2%B3%E5%8D%97_%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3_%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_-_panoramio.jpg //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%E6%B2%B3%E5%8D%97_%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3_%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_-_panoramio.jpg/308px-%E6%B2%B3%E5%8D%97_%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3_%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="154"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The Fengxian cave (c. 675 AD) of the <a href="/wiki/Longmen_Grottoes" title="Longmen Grottoes">Longmen Grottoes</a>, commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Wu_Zetian" title="Wu Zetian">Wu Zetian</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:170px;max-width:170px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:116px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F%EF%BC%8CLuo_Yang_Dragon_Gate_Grottoes_-_panoramio_(9).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1108" data-file-width="1600" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F%EF%BC%8CLuo_Yang_Dragon_Gate_Grottoes_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/252px-%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F%EF%BC%8CLuo_Yang_Dragon_Gate_Grottoes_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F%EF%BC%8CLuo_Yang_Dragon_Gate_Grottoes_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg/336px-%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3%E9%BE%99%E9%97%A8%E7%9F%B3%E7%AA%9F%EF%BC%8CLuo_Yang_Dragon_Gate_Grottoes_-_panoramio_%289%29.jpg 2x" width="168"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Inside a cave of <a href="/wiki/Longmen_Grottoes" title="Longmen Grottoes">Longmen Grottoes</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:118px;max-width:118px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:116px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunhuang_star_map.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2128" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/116px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/174px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/232px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg 2x" width="116"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunhuang_map" title="Dunhuang map">Dunhuang map</a> is to date the world\'s oldest complete preserved star atlas.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Gaozu_of_Tang" title="Emperor Gaozu of Tang">Emperor Gaozu</a> on 18 June 618. It was a <a href="/wiki/Pax_Sinica" title="Pax Sinica">golden age of Chinese civilization</a> and considered to be the most prosperous period of China with significant developments in culture, art, literature, particularly <a href="/wiki/Tang_poetry" title="Tang poetry">poetry</a>, and technology. Buddhism became the predominant religion for the common people. <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>), the national capital, was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">largest city in the world during its time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tang_Protectorates.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="795" data-file-width="1118" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tang_Protectorates.png/220px-Tang_Protectorates.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tang_Protectorates.png/330px-Tang_Protectorates.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tang_Protectorates.png/440px-Tang_Protectorates.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tang_Protectorates.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the six major protectorates during Tang dynasty.</div></div></div>\n<p>The second emperor, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Taizong of Tang">Taizong</a>, is widely regarded as one of the greatest <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">emperors in Chinese history</a>, who had laid the foundation for the dynasty to flourish for centuries beyond his reign. Combined military conquests and diplomatic maneuvers were implemented to eliminate threats from nomadic tribes, extend the border, and submit neighboring states into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Chinese_tributary_system" title="Imperial Chinese tributary system">a tributary system</a>. Military victories in the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty_in_Inner_Asia" title="Tang dynasty in Inner Asia">Tarim Basin</a> kept the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> open, connecting Chang\'an to Central Asia and areas far to the west. In the south, lucrative maritime trade routes began from port cities such as <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>. There was extensive trade with distant foreign countries, and many foreign merchants settled in China, encouraging a cosmopolitan culture. The Tang culture and social systems were observed and imitated by neighboring countries, most notably, <a href="/wiki/Nara_period" title="Nara period">Japan</a>. Internally the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a> linked the political heartland in Chang\'an to the agricultural and economic centers in the eastern and southern parts of the empire. <a href="/wiki/Xuanzang" title="Xuanzang">Xuanzang</a>, a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">Buddhist monk</a>, scholar, traveller, and translator who travelled to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> on his own, and returned with, "over six hundred Mahayana and Hinayana texts, seven statues of the Buddha and more than a hundred <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarira" title="Sarira">sarira</a> relics."\n</p><p>Underlying the prosperity of the early Tang dynasty was a strong centralized bureaucracy with efficient policies. The government was organized as "<a href="/wiki/Three_Departments_and_Six_Ministries" title="Three Departments and Six Ministries">Three Departments and Six Ministries</a>" to separately draft, review, and implement policies. These departments were run by royal family members as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scholar-bureaucrats" title="Scholar-bureaucrats">scholar officials</a> who were selected by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_examination" title="Imperial examination">imperial examinations</a>. These practices, which matured in the Tang dynasty, were continued by the later dynasties, with some modifications.\n</p><p>Under the Tang "<a href="/wiki/Equal-field_system" title="Equal-field system">equal-field system</a>" all land was owned by the Emperor and granted to people according to household size. Men granted land were conscripted for military service for a fixed period each year, a military policy known as the "<a href="/wiki/Fubing_system" title="Fubing system">Fubing system</a>". These policies stimulated a rapid growth in productivity and a significant army without much burden on the state treasury. By the dynasty\'s midpoint, however, <a href="/wiki/Standing_army" title="Standing army">standing armies</a> had replaced conscription, and land was continuously falling into the hands of private owners.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A Tang period <a href="/wiki/Gilding" title="Gilding">gilt</a>-silver jar, shaped in the style of northern <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomad</a>\'s leather bag<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbrey1999127_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbrey1999127-47">[47]</a></sup> decorated with a <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_the_horse" title="Domestication of the horse">horse</a> dancing with a cup of wine in its mouth, as the horses of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xuanzong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Xuanzong of Tang">Emperor Xuanzong</a> were trained to do.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbrey1999127_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbrey1999127-47">[47]</a></sup></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The dynasty continued to flourish under the rule of Empress <a href="/wiki/Wu_Zetian" title="Wu Zetian">Wu Zetian</a>, the only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_regnant" title="Empress regnant">empress regnant</a> in Chinese history, and reached its zenith during the long reign of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xuanzong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Xuanzong of Tang">Emperor Xuanzong</a>, who oversaw an empire that stretched from the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a> with at least 50 million people. There were vibrant artistic and cultural creations, including works of the greatest Chinese <a href="/wiki/Tang_poetry" title="Tang poetry">poets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Li_Bai" title="Li Bai">Li Bai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Du_Fu" title="Du Fu">Du Fu</a>.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;max-width:342px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:82px;max-width:82px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dali_Santa_11.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3328" data-file-width="1872" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Dali_Santa_11.JPG/80px-Dali_Santa_11.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Dali_Santa_11.JPG/120px-Dali_Santa_11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Dali_Santa_11.JPG/160px-Dali_Santa_11.JPG 2x" width="80"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">One of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Pagodas" title="Three Pagodas">Three Pagodas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chong_Shen_Monastery" title="Chong Shen Monastery">Chong Shen Monastery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dali_Town" title="Dali Town">Dali</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:109px;max-width:109px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg"><img alt="&#35199;&#23433;&#22823;&#38593;&#22612;" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg/107px-%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg/161px-%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg/214px-%E8%A5%BF%E5%AE%89%E5%A4%A7%E9%9B%81%E5%A1%94.jpg 2x" width="107"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Giant_Wild_Goose_Pagoda" title="Giant Wild Goose Pagoda">Giant Wild Goose Pagoda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>), built in 652, repaired by Empress Wu Zetian in 704.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:145px;max-width:145px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG"><img alt="Xi\'anwildgoosepagoda2" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="544" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG/143px-Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG/215px-Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG/286px-Xi%27anwildgoosepagoda2.JPG 2x" width="143"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Small_Wild_Goose_Pagoda" title="Small Wild Goose Pagoda">Small Wild Goose Pagoda</a>, built by 709, was adjacent to the Dajianfu Temple in Chang\'an, where Buddhist monks gathered to translate <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> texts into Chinese<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKiang199912_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKiang199912-48">[48]</a></sup></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>At the zenith of prosperity of the empire, the <a href="/wiki/An_Lushan_Rebellion" title="An Lushan Rebellion">An Lushan Rebellion</a> from 755 to 763 was a watershed event that <a href="/wiki/An_Lushan_Rebellion#Death_toll" title="An Lushan Rebellion">devastated the population</a> and drastically weakened the central imperial government. Upon suppression of the rebellion, regional military governors, known as <a href="/wiki/Jiedushi" title="Jiedushi">Jiedushi</a>, gained increasingly autonomous status. With loss of revenue from land tax, the central imperial government relied heavily on <a href="/wiki/Salt_in_Chinese_history" title="Salt in Chinese history">salt monopoly</a>.  Externally, former submissive states raided the empire and the vast border territories were irreversibly lost for subsequent centuries. Nevertheless, civil society recovered and thrived amidst the weakened imperial bureaucracy.\n</p><p>In late Tang period, the empire was worn out by recurring revolts of <a href="/wiki/Jiedushi" title="Jiedushi">regional warlords</a>, while internally, as scholar-officials engaged in fierce <a href="/wiki/Niu%E2%80%93Li_factional_strife" title="Niu&#8211;Li factional strife">factional strife</a>, corrupted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eunuchs" title="Eunuchs">eunuchs</a> <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Dew_incident" title="Sweet Dew incident">amassed immense power</a>. Catastrophically, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huang_Chao_Rebellion" title="Huang Chao Rebellion">Huang Chao Rebellion</a>, from 874 to 884, devastated the entire empire for a decade. The sack of the southern port <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> in 879 was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_massacre" title="Guangzhou massacre">massacre</a> of most of its inhabitants, along with the large foreign merchant enclaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> By 881, both capitals, <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a>, fell successively. The reliance on ethnic <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shatuo" title="Shatuo">Turkic</a> <a href="/wiki/Jiedushi" title="Jiedushi">warlords</a> in suppressing the rebellion increased their power and influence. Consequently, the fall of the dynasty following <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Wen" title="Zhu Wen">Zhu Wen</a>\'s usurpation led to an <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">era of division</a>.\n</p><p>According to historian Mark Edward Lewis:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Most Chinese regard the Tang dynasty (618&#8211;907) as the high point of Imperial China, both politically and culturally. The empire reached its greatest size prior to the Manchu Qing dynasty, becoming the center of an East Asian world linked by religion, script, and many economic and political institutions. Moreover, Tang writers produce the <a href="/wiki/Tang_poetry" title="Tang poetry">finest poetry</a> in China\'s great lyric tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h3><span id="Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_.28AD_907.E2.80.93960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_(AD_907&#8211;960)">Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms (AD 907&#8211;960)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Quanzhou_Kaiyuan_Si_20120229-43.jpg/220px-Quanzhou_Kaiyuan_Si_20120229-43.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Zhenguo Pagoda of <a href="/wiki/Kaiyuan_Temple_(Quanzhou)" title="Kaiyuan Temple (Quanzhou)">Kaiyuan Temple (Quanzhou)</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gongchen_bagoda.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Gongchen_bagoda.JPG/124px-Gongchen_bagoda.JPG" Hangzhou, China</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms (AD 907&#8211;960)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:188px;max-width:188px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:130px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Later_Han.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="1274" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Later_Han.png/186px-Later_Han.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Later_Han.png/279px-Later_Han.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Later_Han.png/372px-Later_Han.png 2x" width="186"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Five Dynasties Ten Kingdoms Period 947 AD</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:100px;max-width:100px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:130px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YunYanSiPagoda.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/YunYanSiPagoda.jpg/98px-YunYanSiPagoda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/YunYanSiPagoda.jpg/147px-YunYanSiPagoda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/YunYanSiPagoda.jpg/196px-YunYanSiPagoda.jpg 2x" width="98"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yunyan_Pagoda" title="Yunyan Pagoda">Yunyan Pagoda</a> in Jiangsu Province of Eastern China.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_(4986578699).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg/192px-096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg/288px-096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg/384px-096_20100911_bt_shanghai_museum_%284986578699%29.jpg 2x" width="192"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Coins of the Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:94px;max-width:94px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1304" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg/92px-Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg/138px-Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg/184px-Gu_Hongzhong_15.jpg 2x" width="92"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Section and detail of <i>Night Revels of <a href="/wiki/Han_Xizai" title="Han Xizai">Han Xizai</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Gu_Hongzhong" title="Gu Hongzhong">Gu Hongzhong</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The period of political disunity between the Tang and the Song, known as the <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period</a>, lasted from 907 to 960. During this half-century, China was in all respects a multi-state system. Five regimes, namely, (Later) <a href="/wiki/Later_Liang_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Liang (Five Dynasties)">Liang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Later_Tang" title="Later Tang">Tang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Later_Jin_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Jin (Five Dynasties)">Jin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Later_Han_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Han (Five Dynasties)">Han</a> and <a href="/wiki/Later_Zhou" title="Later Zhou">Zhou</a>, rapidly succeeded one another in control of the traditional Imperial heartland in northern China. Among the regimes, rulers of (Later) <a href="/wiki/Later_Tang" title="Later Tang">Tang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Later_Jin_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Jin (Five Dynasties)">Jin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Later_Han_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Han (Five Dynasties)">Han</a> were <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicized</a> <a href="/wiki/Shatuo" title="Shatuo">Shatuo Turks</a>, which ruled over the ethnic majority of <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>. More stable and smaller regimes of mostly ethnic <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a> rulers coexisted in south and western China over the period, cumulatively constituted the "Ten Kingdoms".\n</p><p>Amidst political chaos in the north, the strategic <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Prefectures" title="Sixteen Prefectures">Sixteen Prefectures</a> (region along today\'s <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall</a>) were ceded to the emerging <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Khitan Liao dynasty</a>, which drastically weakened the defense of the <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> against northern nomadic empires. To the south, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_B%E1%BA%A1ch_%C4%90%E1%BA%B1ng_(938)" title="Battle of B&#7841;ch &#272;&#7857;ng (938)">gained lasting independence</a> after <a href="/wiki/Third_Chinese_domination_of_Vietnam" title="Third Chinese domination of Vietnam">being a Chinese prefecture</a> for <a href="/wiki/Chinese_domination_of_Vietnam" title="Chinese domination of Vietnam">many centuries</a>. With wars dominated in Northern China, there were mass southward migrations of population, which further enhanced the southward shift of cultural and economic centers in China. The <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">era</a> ended with the coup of <a href="/wiki/Later_Zhou" title="Later Zhou">Later Zhou</a> general <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizu_of_Song" title="Emperor Taizu of Song">Zhao Kuangyin</a>, and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> in 960, which eventually annihilated the remains of the "Ten Kingdoms" and reunified China.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Song.2C_Liao.2C_Jin.2C_and_Western_Xia_dynasties_.28AD_960.E2.80.931234.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Song,_Liao,_Jin,_and_Western_Xia_dynasties_(AD_960&#8211;1234)">Song, Liao, Jin, and Western Xia dynasties (AD 960&#8211;1234)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Song_dynasty" from the <i><a href="/wiki/Wujing_Zongyao" title="Wujing Zongyao">Wujing Zongyao</a></i> of 1044 AD.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>In 960, the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizu_of_Song" title="Emperor Taizu of Song">Emperor Taizu</a>, with its capital established in <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a> (also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bianjing" title="Bianjing">Bianjing</a>). In 979, the Song dynasty reunified most of the <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a>, while large swaths of the outer territories were occupied by <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicized</a> <a href="/wiki/Nomadic_empire" title="Nomadic empire">nomadic empires</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Khitan_people" title="Khitan people">Khitan</a> <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a>, which lasted from 907 to 1125, ruled over <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">Northern China</a>. Meanwhile, in what are now the north-western Chinese provinces of <a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> tribes founded the <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia dynasty</a> from 1032 to 1227.\n</p><p>Aiming to recover the strategic <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Prefectures" title="Sixteen Prefectures">Sixteen Prefectures</a> lost in the <a href="/wiki/Later_Jin_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Jin (Five Dynasties)">previous dynasty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaoliang_River" title="Battle of Gaoliang River">campaigns</a> were launched against the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizong_of_Song" title="Emperor Taizong of Song">early Song period</a>, which all ended in failure. Then in 1004, the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao</a> <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> swept over the exposed <a href="/wiki/North_China_Plain" title="North China Plain">North China Plain</a> and reached the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a>, forcing the Song\'s submission and then agreement to the <a href="/wiki/Chanyuan_Treaty" title="Chanyuan Treaty">Chanyuan Treaty</a>, which imposed heavy annual tributes from the Song treasury. The treaty was a significant reversal of Chinese dominance of the traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Chinese_tributary_system" title="Imperial Chinese tributary system">tributary system</a>. Yet the annual outflow of Song\'s silver to the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao</a> was paid back through the purchase of Chinese goods and products, which expanded the Song economy, and replenished its treasury. This dampened the incentive for the Song to further campaign against the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao</a>. Meanwhile, this cross-border trade and contact induced further <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicization</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao Empire</a>, at the expense of its military might which was derived from its primitive nomadic lifestyle. Similar treaties and social-economical consequences occurred in Song\'s relations with the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a>.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dingzhou_Liaodi_Pagoda_3.jpg/248px-Dingzhou_Liaodi_Pagoda_3.jpg 2x" width="124"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Liaodi_Pagoda" title="Liaodi Pagoda">Liaodi Pagoda</a>, Song dynasty</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:112px;max-width:112px"><div class="thumbimage" 2x" width="110"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Pagoda of <a href="/wiki/Tianning_Temple_(Beijing)" title="Tianning Temple (Beijing)">Tianing Temple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liao_Dynasty" title="Liao Dynasty">Liao Dynasty</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:119px;max-width:119px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:156px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg/117px-Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg/176px-Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg/234px-Hohhot_White_Pagoda_2.jpg 2x" width="117"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Ten Thousand Copies of the Huayan Sutra Pagoda, commonly known as the White Pagoda, Liao dynasty</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:119px;max-width:119px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:156px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg/117px-Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg/176px-Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg/234px-Poyang_Yongfu_Si_Ta_2017.11.25_10-04-37.jpg 2x" width="117"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Poyang Yongfu Temple Pagoda, Song dynasty</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Within the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchen</a> tribes revolted against their overlords to establish the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a> in 1115. In 1125, the devastating <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin</a> <a href="/wiki/Cataphract" title="Cataphract">cataphract</a> annihilated the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a>, while remnants of <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao</a> court members fled to Central Asia to found the <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai Empire (Western Liao dynasty)</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jin%E2%80%93Song_Wars" title="Jin&#8211;Song Wars">Jin\'s invasion of the Song dynasty</a> followed swiftly. In 1127, <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a> was sacked, a massive catastrophe known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jingkang_Incident" title="Jingkang Incident">Jingkang Incident</a>, ending the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Song_dynasty" title="Northern Song dynasty">Northern Song dynasty</a>. Later the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurchen_campaigns_against_the_Song_dynasty" title="Jurchen campaigns against the Song dynasty">entire north of China was conquered</a>. The survived members of Song court regrouped in the new capital city of <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, and initiated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song_dynasty" title="Southern Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a>, which ruled territories south of the <a href="/wiki/Huai_River" title="Huai River">Huai River</a>. In the ensuing years, the territory and population of China were divided between the Song dynasty, the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia dynasty</a>. The era ended with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest" title="Mongol conquest">Mongol conquest</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a> fell in 1227, the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Jin_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Jin dynasty">Jin dynasty</a> in 1234, and finally the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a> in 1279.\n</p><p>Despite its military weakness, the Song dynasty is widely considered to be the high point of classical Chinese civilization. The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Economy of the Song dynasty">Song economy</a>, facilitated by technology advancement, had reached a level of sophistication probably unseen in world history before its time. The population soared to over 100 million and the living standards of common people improved tremendously due to improvements in rice cultivation and the wide availability of coal for production. The capital cities of <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a> and subsequently <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a> were both the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">most populous cities</a> in the world for their time, and encouraged vibrant civil societies unmatched by previous Chinese dynasties. Although land trading routes to the far west were blocked by nomadic empires, there were extensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_Silk_Route" title="Maritime Silk Route">maritime trade</a> with neighbouring states, which facilitated the use of Song coinage as the de facto currency of exchange. Giant wooden vessels equipped with <a href="/wiki/Compass" title="Compass">compasses</a> travelled throughout the <a href="/wiki/China_Seas" title="China Seas">China Seas</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. The concept of <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a> was practised by merchants to hedge the risks of such long-haul maritime <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shipment" title="Shipment">shipments</a>. With prosperous economic activities, the historically first use of <a href="/wiki/Jiaozi_(currency)" title="Jiaozi (currency)">paper currency</a> emerged in the western city of <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, as a supplement to the existing copper <a href="/wiki/Coin" title="Coin">coins</a>.\n</p><p>The Song dynasty was considered to be the golden age of great advancements in science and technology of China, thanks to innovative scholar-officials such as <a href="/wiki/Su_Song" title="Su Song">Su Song</a> (1020&#8211;1101) and <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">Shen Kuo</a> (1031&#8211;1095). Inventions such as the hydro-mechanical astronomical clock, the first continuous and endless power-transmitting chain, <a href="/wiki/Woodblock_printing" title="Woodblock printing">woodblock printing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paper_money" title="Paper money">paper money</a> were all invented during the Song dynasty.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:492px;max-width:492px"><div class="tsingle" style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:358px;max-width:358px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:83px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image"
