width="128"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">City views of Song dynasty from paintings. Clockwise from upper left: A Northern Song Dynasty (960-1127) era Chinese painting of a water-powered mill for grain, with surrounding river transport. The bridge scene from <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zeduan" title="Zhang Zeduan">Zhang Zeduan</a>\'s (1085&#8211;1145) painting <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Along_the_River_During_Qingming_Festival" title="Along the River During Qingming Festival">Along the River During Qingming Festival</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">Chinese boats</a> from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Along_the_River_During_Qingming_Festival" title="Along the River During Qingming Festival">Along the River During Qingming Festival</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Leifeng_Pagoda" title="Leifeng Pagoda">Leifeng Pagoda</a> in the Southern Song Dynasty by <a href="/wiki/Li_Song_(painter)" title="Li Song (painter)">Li Song</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>There was court intrigue between the political reformers and conservatives, led by the chancellors <a href="/wiki/Wang_Anshi" title="Wang Anshi">Wang Anshi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sima_Guang" title="Sima Guang">Sima Guang</a>, respectively. By the mid-to-late 13th century, the Chinese had adopted the dogma of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Confucian" title="Neo-Confucian">Neo-Confucian</a> philosophy formulated by <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Xi" title="Zhu Xi">Zhu Xi</a>. Enormous literary works were compiled during the Song dynasty, such as the historical work, the <i><a href="/wiki/Zizhi_Tongjian" title="Zizhi Tongjian">Zizhi Tongjian</a></i> ("Comprehensive Mirror to Aid in Government"). The invention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodblock_print" title="Woodblock print">movable-type printing</a> further facilitated the spread of knowledge. Culture and the arts flourished, with grandiose artworks such as <i><a href="/wiki/Along_the_River_During_the_Qingming_Festival" title="Along the River During the Qingming Festival">Along the River During the Qingming Festival</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Eighteen_Songs_of_a_Nomad_Flute" title="Eighteen Songs of a Nomad Flute">Eighteen Songs of a Nomad Flute</a></i>, along with great Buddhist painters such as the prolific <a href="/wiki/Lin_Tinggui" title="Lin Tinggui">Lin Tinggui</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> was also a period of major innovation in the <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">history of warfare</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">Gunpowder</a>, while invented in the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a>, was first put into use in battlefields by the Song army, inspiring a succession of new <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_engine" title="Siege engine">siege engines</a> designs. During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song_dynasty" title="Southern Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a>, as its survival hinged decisively on guarding the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huai_River" title="Huai River">Huai River</a> against the cavalry forces from the north, the first standing navy in China was assembled in 1132, with its <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">admiral</a>\'s headquarters established at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinghai" title="Dinghai">Dinghai</a>. <a href="/wiki/Paddle_wheel" title="Paddle wheel">Paddle-wheel</a> warships equipped with <a href="/wiki/Trebuchet" title="Trebuchet">trebuchets</a> could launch <a href="/wiki/Incendiary_device" title="Incendiary device">incendiary bombs</a> made of <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> and lime, as recorded in Song\'s victory over the invading <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin</a> forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tangdao" title="Battle of Tangdao">Battle of Tangdao</a> in the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Caishi" title="Battle of Caishi">Battle of Caishi</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze River</a> in 1161.\n</p><p>The advances in civilization during the Song dynasty came to an abrupt end following the devastating <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Song dynasty">Mongol conquest</a>, during which the population sharply dwindled, with a marked contraction in economy. Despite viciously <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Song dynasty">halting Mongol advance</a> for more than three decades, the Southern Song capital <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a> fell in 1276, followed by the final annihilation of the Song standing navy at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yamen" title="Battle of Yamen">Battle of Yamen</a> in 1279.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Yuan_dynasty_.28AD_1271.E2.80.931368.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Yuan_dynasty_(AD_1271&#8211;1368)">Yuan dynasty (AD 1271&#8211;1368)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikh_Mongol_Uls" title="Ikh Mongol Uls">Ikh Mongol Uls</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Yuan dynasty (AD 1271&#8211;1368)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:95px;max-width:95px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:140px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="448" data-file-width="297" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg/93px-Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg/140px-Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg/186px-Miaoyingsi_baita.jpg 2x" width="93"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The White Stupa of <a href="/wiki/Miaoying_Temple" title="Miaoying Temple">Miaoying Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:193px;max-width:193px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:140px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1889" data-file-width="2579" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg/191px-Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg/287px-Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg/382px-Deva_King_of_the_East.jpg 2x" width="191"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Four_Heavenly_Kings" title="Four Heavenly Kings">Deva King of the East</a> on the east wall of the <a href="/wiki/Cloud_Platform_at_Juyong_Pass" title="Cloud Platform at Juyong Pass">Cloud Platform at Juyong Pass</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:170px;max-width:170px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:84px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1359" data-file-width="2688" decoding="async" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg/168px-Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg/252px-Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg/336px-Bronze_cannon_of_1332.jpg 2x" width="168"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Yuan period <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearm</a> with inscription dated the 3rd year of the Zhiyuan era (1332). Yuan Dynasty (1206-1368). Discovered at the Yunju Temple, Fangshan, Beijing, 1935.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:118px;max-width:118px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:84px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1918" data-file-width="2631" decoding="async" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg/116px-Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg/174px-Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg/232px-Yuan_dynasty_banknote_with_its_printing_plate_1287.jpg 2x" width="116"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Yuan dynasty banknote with its printing wood plate, 1287 AD.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolMap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="609" data-file-width="1132" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MongolMap.jpg/330px-MongolMap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MongolMap.jpg/495px-MongolMap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MongolMap.jpg/660px-MongolMap.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolMap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mongol successor khanates</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> was formally proclaimed in 1271, when the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mongol_rulers" title="List of Mongol rulers">Great Khan of Mongol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, one of the grandsons of <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>, assumed the additional title of the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">Emperor of China</a>, and considered <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">his inherited part</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_dynasty" title="Chinese dynasty">Chinese dynasty</a>. In the preceding decades, the Mongols had conquered the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a> in Northern China, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song_dynasty" title="Southern Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a> fell in 1279 after a <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Song dynasty">protracted and bloody war</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongol</a> Yuan dynasty became the first <a href="/wiki/Conquest_dynasty" title="Conquest dynasty">conquest dynasty</a> in Chinese history to rule the entire <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_China" title="List of ethnic groups in China">its population</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Mongols_in_China" title="Mongols in China">ethnic minority</a>. The dynasty also directly controlled the <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolian</a> heartland and other regions, inheriting the largest share of territory of the <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">divided Mongol Empire</a>, which roughly coincided with the modern area of China and nearby regions in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>. Further expansion of the empire was halted after defeats in the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">invasions of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Vietnam" title="Mongol invasions of Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. Following the previous <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a>, the capital of Yuan dynasty was established at <a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Khanbaliq</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Dadu</a>, modern-day <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a> was reconstructed to connect the remote capital city to economic hubs in southern part of China, setting the precedence and foundation where <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> would largely remain as the <a href="/wiki/Historical_capitals_of_China" title="Historical capitals of China">capital</a> of the successive regimes that unified China mainland.\n</p><p>After the peace treaty in <a href="/wiki/Kaidu%E2%80%93Kublai_war" title="Kaidu&#8211;Kublai war">1304</a> that ended a series of <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire#Civil_war" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">Mongols civil wars</a>, the emperors of the Yuan dynasty were upheld as the nominal <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">Great Khan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">Khagan</a>) of the greater <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> over other <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Mongol Khanates</a>, which nonetheless remained <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">de facto autonomous</a>. The era was known as <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a></i>, when much of the <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian continent</a> was ruled by the Mongols. For the first and only time in history, the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">silk road</a> was controlled entirely by a single state, facilitating the flow of people, trade, and cultural exchange. Network of roads and a <a href="/wiki/Yam_(route)" title="Yam (route)">postal system</a> were established to connect the vast empire. Lucrative maritime trade, developed from the previous <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, continued to flourish, with <a href="/wiki/Quanzhou" title="Quanzhou">Quanzhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a> emerging as the largest ports in the world. Adventurous travelers from the far west, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a>, would have settled in China for decades. Upon his return, his detail <a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">travel record</a> inspired generations of <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">medieval Europeans</a> with the splendors of the far East. The Yuan dynasty was the first ancient economy, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paper_currency" title="Paper currency">paper currency</a>, known at the time as <a href="/wiki/Chao_(currency)" title="Chao (currency)">Chao</a>, was used as the predominant medium of exchange. Its unrestricted issuance in the late Yuan dynasty inflicted <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflation</a>, which eventually brought the downfall of the dynasty.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:190px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Observatory,_Dengfeng,_2015-09-24_08.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4256" data-file-width="2832" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg/127px-The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg/191px-The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg/254px-The_Observatory%2C_Dengfeng%2C_2015-09-24_08.jpg 2x" width="127"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dengfeng_Observatory" title="Dengfeng Observatory">Dengfeng Observatory</a>, the first in a series of 27 astronomical observatories built in the early Yuan dynasty.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:109px;max-width:109px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:190px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3968" data-file-width="2232" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg/107px-%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg/161px-%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg/214px-%E6%9F%8F%E6%9E%97%E7%A6%85%E5%AF%BA%E8%88%8D%E5%88%A9%E5%A1%94_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="107"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Pagoda of Bailin Temple, an octagonal-based brick pagoda built in 1330 during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Jayaatu_Khan_Tugh_Tem%C3%BCr" title="Jayaatu Khan Tugh Tem&#252;r">Emperor Wenzong</a>, ruler of the Mongol-led Yuan Dynasty (1271&#8211;1368).</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>While the Mongol rulers of the Yuan dynasty adopted substantially to Chinese culture, their <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicization</a> was of lesser extent compared to earlier <a href="/wiki/Conquest_dynasty" title="Conquest dynasty">conquest dynasties</a> in Chinese history. For preserving racial superiority as the conqueror and ruling class, traditional nomadic customs and heritage from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_Steppe" title="Mongolian Steppe">Mongolian steppe</a> were held in high regard. On the other hand, the Mongol rulers also adopted flexibly to a variety of cultures from many advanced civilizations within the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">vast empire</a>. Traditional social structure and culture in China underwent immense transform during the Mongol dominance. Large group of <a href="/wiki/Semu" title="Semu">foreign migrants</a> settled in China, who enjoyed elevated social status over the majority <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>, while enriching Chinese culture with foreign elements. The class of <a href="/wiki/Scholar-official" title="Scholar-official">scholar officials</a> and intellectuals, traditional bearers of elite Chinese culture, lost substantial social status. This stimulated the development of culture of the common folks. There were prolific works in <a href="/wiki/Zaju" title="Zaju">zaju variety shows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanqu" title="Sanqu">literary songs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sanqu" title="Sanqu">sanqu</a>), which were written in a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Yuan_poetry" title="Yuan poetry">poetry style</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Qu_(poetry)" title="Qu (poetry)">qu</a>. <a href="/wiki/Novel" title="Novel">Novels</a> of vernacular style gained unprecedented status and popularity.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:112px;max-width:112px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:164px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="569" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg/110px-%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg/165px-%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg/220px-%E4%BB%A3%E5%8E%BF%E9%98%BF%E8%82%B2%E7%8E%8B%E5%A1%94.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Ayuwang_Pagoda" title="Ayuwang Pagoda">Ayuwang Stupa</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Shanxi" title="Shanxi">Shanxi</a>, China.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:164px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="3240" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG/124px-Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG/186px-Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG/248px-Zhao_guan_Tower_2011-10.JPG 2x" width="124"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">stupa</a> on top of an arch (<i>crossing street tower</i>), is a common form of architecture during Yuan period.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Before the Mongol invasion, Chinese dynasties reported approximately 120 million inhabitants; after the conquest had been completed in 1279, the 1300 census reported roughly 60 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> This major decline is not necessarily due only to Mongol killings. Scholars such as Frederick W. Mote argue that the wide drop in numbers reflects an administrative failure to record rather than an actual decrease; others such as <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Brook" title="Timothy Brook">Timothy Brook</a> argue that the Mongols created a system of <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">enserfment</a> among a huge portion of the Chinese populace, causing many to disappear from the census altogether; other historians including William McNeill and David Morgan consider that <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> was the main factor behind the demographic decline during this period. In the 14th century China suffered additional depredations from epidemics of plague, estimated to have killed 25 million people, 30% of the population of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout the Yuan dynasty, there was some general sentiment among the populace against the Mongol dominance. Yet rather than the nationalist cause, it was mainly strings of natural disasters and incompetent governance that triggered widespread peasant uprisings since the 1340s. After the <a href="/wiki/Largest_naval_battle_in_history" title="Largest naval battle in history">massive naval engagement</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Poyang" title="Battle of Lake Poyang">at Lake Poyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Zhu Yuanzhang</a> prevailed over other rebel forces in the south. He proclaimed himself <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">emperor</a> and founded the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> in 1368. The same year his northern expedition army captured the capital <a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Khanbaliq</a>. The Yuan remnants fled back to <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Yuan_dynasty" title="Northern Yuan dynasty">sustained the regime</a>. Other <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Khanates</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> continued to exist after the fall of <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> in China.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Ming_dynasty_.28AD_1368.E2.80.931644.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ming_dynasty_(AD_1368&#8211;1644)">Ming dynasty (AD 1368&#8211;1644)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ming_dynasty" title="History of the Ming dynasty">History of the Ming dynasty</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Dongyang_Luzhai_2015.05.24_15-53-48.jpg/300px-Dongyang_Luzhai_2015.05.24_15-53-48.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Dongyang_Luzhai_2015.05.24_15-53-48.jpg/400px-Dongyang_Luzhai_2015.05.24_15-53-48.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" during the early Ming dynasty</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fenghuang_old_town.JPG"><img alt="Fenghuang old town" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Fenghuang_old_town.JPG/200px-Fenghuang_old_town.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Fenghuang_old_town.JPG/300px-Fenghuang_old_town.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Fenghuang_old_town.JPG/400px-Fenghuang_old_town.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Fenghuang_County" title="Fenghuang County">Fenghuang County</a>, an ancient town that harbors many architectural remains of Ming and Qing styles.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg"><img alt="Yixian Hongcun" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg/200px-Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg/300px-Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg/400px-Yixian_Hongcun_2016.09.09_17-27-03.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Hongcun" title="Hongcun">Hongcun</a>, a village in Yi County in the historical Huizhou region of southern Anhui Province.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinye-9.jpg"><img alt="Xinye" data-file-height="2245" data-file-width="3991" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Xinye-9.jpg/200px-Xinye-9.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Xinye-9.jpg/300px-Xinye-9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Xinye-9.jpg/400px-Xinye-9.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Xinye_Village" title="Xinye Village">Xinye</a>, a village noted for its well-preserved Ming and Qing era architecture and ancient residential buildings.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> was founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhu_Yuanzhang" title="Zhu Yuanzhang">Zhu Yuanzhang</a> in 1368, who proclaimed himself as the <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu Emperor</a>. The capital was initially set at <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, and was later moved to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> from <a href="/wiki/Yongle_Emperor" title="Yongle Emperor">Yongle Emperor\'s</a> reign onward.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3666" data-file-width="5016" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nieuhof-Ambassade-vers-la-Chine-1665_0789.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porcelain_Tower" title="Porcelain Tower">Porcelain Tower</a>, from <i><a href="/wiki/An_embassy_from_the_East-India_Company" title="An embassy from the East-India Company">An embassy from the East-India Company</a></i> (1665) by Johan Nieuhof . It was first discovered by the Western world when travelers like <a href="/wiki/Johan_Nieuhof" title="Johan Nieuhof">Johan Nieuhof</a> visited it, sometimes listing it as one of the Seven Wonders of the World.</div></div></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haihui_Temple_(Shanxi).JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="4032" data-file-width="3024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG/124px-Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG/186px-Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG/248px-Haihui_Temple_%28Shanxi%29.JPG 2x" width="124"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Haihui Temple Pagodas, built in the Ming period.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:112px;max-width:112px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5472" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg/110px-Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg/165px-Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg/220px-Jining_Chongjue_Si_Tieta_2015.08.13_17-18-45.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Pagoda of Chongjue Temple, dated to the Song dynasty. The onion-shaped <a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Drin" title="S&#333;rin">S&#333;rin</a> was a Ming dynasty addition.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Urbanization increased as the population grew and as the division of labor grew more complex. Large urban centers, such as <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, also contributed to the growth of private industry. In particular, small-scale industries grew up, often specializing in paper, silk, cotton, and porcelain goods. For the most part, however, relatively small urban centers with markets proliferated around the country. Town markets mainly traded food, with some necessary manufactures such as pins or oil.\n</p><p>Despite the <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a> and intellectual introspection characteristic of the increasingly popular new school of <a href="/wiki/Neo-Confucianism" title="Neo-Confucianism">neo-Confucianism</a>, China under the early Ming dynasty was not isolated. Foreign trade and other contacts with the outside world, particularly Japan, increased considerably. Chinese merchants explored all of the Indian Ocean, reaching East Africa with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treasure_voyages" title="Treasure voyages">voyages of Zheng He</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu Emperor</a>, being the only founder of a <a href="/wiki/Dynasties_in_Chinese_history" title="Dynasties in Chinese history">Chinese dynasty</a> who was also of peasant origin, had laid the foundation of a state that relied fundamentally in agriculture. Commerce and trade, which flourished in the previous <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan</a> dynasties, were less emphasized. Neo-feudal landholdings of the Song and Mongol periods were expropriated by the Ming rulers. Land estates were confiscated by the government, fragmented, and rented out. Private slavery was forbidden. Consequently, after the death of the <a href="/wiki/Yongle_Emperor" title="Yongle Emperor">Yongle Emperor</a>, independent peasant landholders predominated in Chinese agriculture. These laws might have paved the way to removing the worst of the poverty during the previous regimes. Towards later era of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>, with declining government control, commerce, trade and private industries revived.\n</p><p>The dynasty had a strong and complex central government that unified and controlled the empire. The emperor\'s role became more autocratic, although <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu Emperor</a> necessarily continued to use what he called the "<a href="/wiki/Grand_Secretariat" title="Grand Secretariat">Grand Secretariat</a>" to assist with the immense paperwork of the bureaucracy, including <a href="/wiki/Memorial_to_the_throne" title="Memorial to the throne">memorials</a> (petitions and recommendations to the throne), imperial edicts in reply, reports of various kinds, and tax records. It was this same bureaucracy that later prevented the Ming government from being able to adapt to changes in society, and eventually led to its decline.\n</p><p>The Yongle Emperor strenuously tried to extend China\'s influence beyond its borders by demanding other rulers send ambassadors to China to present tribute. A large navy was built, including four-masted ships displacing 1,500&#160;tons. A standing army of 1 million troops was created. The Chinese armies <a href="/wiki/Ming%E2%80%93H%E1%BB%93_War" title="Ming&#8211;H&#7891; War">conquered</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Chinese_domination_of_Vietnam" title="Fourth Chinese domination of Vietnam">occupied Vietnam</a> for around 20 years, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treasure_voyages" title="Treasure voyages">Chinese fleet sailed</a> the China seas and the Indian Ocean, cruising as far as the east coast of Africa. The Chinese gained influence in eastern <a href="/wiki/Moghulistan" title="Moghulistan">Moghulistan</a>. Several maritime Asian nations sent envoys with tribute for the Chinese emperor. Domestically, the Grand Canal was expanded and became a stimulus to domestic trade. Over 100,000&#160;tons of iron per year were produced. Many books were printed using movable type. The imperial palace in Beijing\'s <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a> reached its current splendor. It was also during these centuries that the potential of south China came to be fully exploited. New crops were widely cultivated and industries such as those producing porcelain and textiles flourished.\n</p><p>In 1449 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esen_Tayisi" title="Esen Tayisi">Esen Tayisi</a> led an <a href="/wiki/Oirats" title="Oirats">Oirat</a> Mongol invasion of northern China which culminated in the capture of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhengtong_Emperor" title="Zhengtong Emperor">Zhengtong Emperor</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tumu_Fortress" title="Battle of Tumu Fortress">Tumu</a>. Since then, the Ming became on the defensive on the northern frontier, which led to the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Great_Wall" title="Ming Great Wall">Ming Great Wall</a> being built. Most of what remains of the Great Wall of China today was either built or repaired by the Ming. The brick and granite work was enlarged, the watchtowers were redesigned, and cannons were placed along its length.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:155px;max-width:155px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:254px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg"><img alt="A donkey" data-file-height="1618" data-file-width="976" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg/153px-Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg/230px-Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg/306px-Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg 2x" width="153"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Eagles</i> by <a href="/wiki/Lin_Liang" title="Lin Liang">Lin Liang</a>. Located at the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:254px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg"><img alt="A trout" data-file-height="2116" data-file-width="1254" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg/151px-Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg/227px-Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg/302px-Bian_Jingzhao-Snow_Plum_and_Twin_Cranes.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Snow Plums and Twin Cranes</i> by <a href="/wiki/Bian_Jingzhao" title="Bian Jingzhao">Bian Jingzhao</a>. Located at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guangdong_Provincial_Museum" title="Guangdong Provincial Museum">Guangdong Provincial Museum</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>At sea, the Ming became increasingly isolationist after the death of the Yongle Emperor. The treasure voyages which sailed Indian Ocean were discontinued, and the <a href="/wiki/Haijin" title="Haijin">maritime prohibition</a> laws were set in place banning the Chinese from sailing abroad. European traders who reached China in the midst of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> were repeatedly rebuked in their requests for trade, with the Portuguese being <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tunmen" title="Battle of Tunmen">repulsed by the Ming navy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tuen_Mun" title="Tuen Mun">Tuen Mun</a> in 1521 and again <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Tamao" title="Second Battle of Tamao">in 1522</a>. Domestic and foreign demands for overseas trade, deemed illegal by the state, led to widespread <i><a href="/wiki/Wokou" title="Wokou">wokou</a></i> piracy attacking the southeastern coastline during the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_Emperor" title="Jiajing Emperor">Jiajing Emperor</a> (1507&#8211;1567), which only subsided after the opening of ports in <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_wokou_raids" title="Jiajing wokou raids">much military suppression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The Portuguese were allowed to settle in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> in 1557 for trade, which remained in Portuguese hands until 1999. The Dutch entry into the Chinese seas was also met with fierce resistance, with the Dutch being chased off the <a href="/wiki/Penghu" title="Penghu">Penghu islands</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-Dutch_conflicts" title="Sino-Dutch conflicts">Sino-Dutch conflicts</a> of 1622&#8211;1624 and were forced to settle in Taiwan instead. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">The Dutch in Taiwan</a> fought with the Ming in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Liaoluo_Bay" title="Battle of Liaoluo Bay">Battle of Liaoluo Bay</a> in 1633 and lost, and eventually surrendered to the Ming loyalist <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> in 1662, after the fall of the Ming dynasty.\n</p><p>In 1556, during the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_Emperor" title="Jiajing Emperor">Jiajing Emperor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1556_Shaanxi_earthquake" title="1556 Shaanxi earthquake">Shaanxi earthquake</a> killed about 830,000 people, the deadliest earthquake of all time.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> intervened deeply in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_invasions_of_Korea_(1592%E2%80%9398)" title="Japanese invasions of Korea (1592&#8211;98)">Japanese invasions of Korea (1592&#8211;98)</a>, which ended with the withdrawal of all invading Japanese forces in <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, and the restoration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseon_dynasty" title="Joseon dynasty">Joseon dynasty</a>, its traditional ally and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tributaries_of_Imperial_China" title="List of tributaries of Imperial China">tributary state</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Chinese_tributary_system" title="Imperial Chinese tributary system">regional hegemony</a> of the Ming dynasty was preserved at a toll on its resources. Coincidentally, with <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming</a>\'s control in <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> in decline, the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchen</a>) tribes, under their chieftain <a href="/wiki/Nurhaci" title="Nurhaci">Nurhaci</a>, broke away from Ming\'s rule, and emerged as a powerful, unified state, which was <a href="/wiki/Hong_Taiji" title="Hong Taiji">later proclaimed</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>. It went on to subdue the much weakened <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseon_dynasty" title="Joseon dynasty">Korea</a> as its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tributaries_of_Imperial_China" title="List of tributaries of Imperial China">tributary</a>, conquered <a href="/wiki/Northern_Yuan_dynasty" title="Northern Yuan dynasty">Mongolia</a>, and expanded its territory to the outskirt of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall</a>. The most elite army of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> was to station at the <a href="/wiki/Shanhai_Pass" title="Shanhai Pass">Shanhai Pass</a> to guard the last stronghold against the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchus</a>, which weakened its suppression of internal <a href="/wiki/Li_Zicheng" title="Li Zicheng">peasants uprisings</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Qing_dynasty_.28AD_1644.E2.80.931911.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Qing_dynasty_(AD_1644&#8211;1911)">Qing dynasty (AD 1644&#8211;1911)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Century_of_humiliation" title="Century of humiliation">Century of humiliation</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Putuo_Zongcheng_Temple.jpg"><img alt="XiAn CityWall DiLou" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Putuo_Zongcheng_Temple.jpg/400px-Putuo_Zongcheng_Temple.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Putuo_Zongcheng_Temple" title="Putuo Zongcheng Temple">Putuo Zongcheng Temple</a>, a Buddhist temple complex built between 1767 and 1771. The temple was modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Potala_Palace" title="Potala Palace">Potala Palace</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%99%8B%E5%9F%8E%E7%9A%87%E5%9F%8E%E7%9B%B8%E5%BA%9C_-_panoramio_(14).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="133"
