2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Huangcheng_Chancellor" title="House of the Huangcheng Chancellor">House of the Huangcheng Chancellor</a>, a 10-hectare walled estate on Phoenix Hill in southeastern <a href="/wiki/Shanxi" title="Shanxi">Shanxi</a>, China.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg/200px-%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg/300px-%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg/400px-%E8%8A%B1%E6%88%8F%E6%A5%BC_%E5%B1%B1%E9%97%A8_%E5%89%AF%E6%9C%AC.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Flower Theatre, a Qing period guildhall.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg/200px-%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg/300px-%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg/400px-%E4%BC%9A%E8%8A%B3.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A residential building of <a href="/wiki/Qiao_Family_Compound" title="Qiao Family Compound">Qiao Family Compound</a>, built in the Qing period.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> (1644&#8211;1911) was the last imperial dynasty in China. Founded by the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchus</a>, it was the second <a href="/wiki/Conquest_dynasty" title="Conquest dynasty">conquest dynasty</a> to rule  the entire territory of China and its people. The Manchus were formerly known as <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchens</a>, residing in the northeastern part of the Ming territory outside the Great Wall. They emerged as the major threat to the late Ming dynasty after <a href="/wiki/Nurhaci" title="Nurhaci">Nurhaci</a> united all Jurchen tribes and established an independent state. However, the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> would be overthrown by <a href="/wiki/Li_Zicheng" title="Li Zicheng">Li Zicheng</a>\'s peasants rebellion, with Beijing captured in 1644 and the <a href="/wiki/Chongzhen_Emperor" title="Chongzhen Emperor">Chongzhen Emperor</a>, the last Ming emperor, committing suicide. The Manchus allied with the former Ming general <a href="/wiki/Wu_Sangui" title="Wu Sangui">Wu Sangui</a> to seize Beijing, which was made the capital of the Qing dynasty, and then proceeded to subdue the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Ming_dynasty" title="Southern Ming dynasty">Ming remnants in the south</a>. The decades of Manchu conquest caused <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_and_anthropogenic_disasters_by_death_toll#Wars_and_armed_conflicts" title="List of wars and anthropogenic disasters by death toll">enormous loss of lives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_China_before_1912#Qing_dynasty_(1644&#8211;1912)" title="Economic history of China before 1912">economic scale of China shrank drastically</a>. In total, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_conquest_of_the_Ming" title="Qing conquest of the Ming">Qing conquest of the Ming</a> (1618&#8211;1683) cost as many as 25 million lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Manchus adopted the Confucian norms of traditional Chinese government in their rule and were considered a Chinese dynasty.\n</p><p>The Manchus enforced a \'queue order,\' forcing the Han Chinese to adopt the Manchu <a href="/wiki/Queue_(hairstyle)" title="Queue (hairstyle)">queue hairstyle</a>. Officials were required to wear Manchu-style clothing <i><a href="/wiki/Changshan" title="Changshan">Changshan</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Eight_Banners" title="Eight Banners">bannermen</a> dress and <i><a href="/wiki/Tangzhuang" title="Tangzhuang">Tangzhuang</a></i>), but ordinary Han civilians were allowed to wear traditional Han clothing, or <i><a href="/wiki/Hanfu" title="Hanfu">Hanfu</a></i>. Most Han then voluntarily shifted to wearing Qipao anyway. The <a href="/wiki/Kangxi_Emperor" title="Kangxi Emperor">Kangxi Emperor</a> ordered the creation of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kangxi_Dictionary" title="Kangxi Dictionary">Kangxi Dictionary</a></i>, the most complete dictionary of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Chinese characters</a> that had been compiled. The Qing dynasty set up the <a href="/wiki/Eight_Banners" title="Eight Banners">Eight Banners</a> system that provided the basic framework for the Qing military organization. Bannermen could not undertake trade or manual labor; they had to petition to be removed from banner status. They were considered a form of nobility and were given preferential treatment in terms of annual pensions, land, and allotments of cloth.\n</p><p>Over the next half-century, all areas previously under the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> were consolidated under the Qing. <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, Tibet, and <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> were also formally incorporated into Chinese territory. Between 1673 and 1681, the Kangxi Emperor suppressed the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Three_Feudatories" title="Revolt of the Three Feudatories">Revolt of the Three Feudatories</a>, an uprising of three generals in Southern China who had been denied hereditary rule of large fiefdoms granted by the <a href="/wiki/Shunzhi_Emperor" title="Shunzhi Emperor">previous emperor</a>. In 1683, the Qing staged an amphibious assault on southern <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, bringing down the rebel <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tungning" title="Kingdom of Tungning">Kingdom of Tungning</a>, which was founded by the Ming loyalist <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> (Zheng Chenggong) in 1662 after the fall of the Southern Ming, and had served as a base for continued Ming resistance in Southern China. The Qing <a href="/wiki/Sino-Russian_border_conflicts" title="Sino-Russian border conflicts">defeated the Russians at Albazin</a>, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nerchinsk" title="Treaty of Nerchinsk">Treaty of Nerchinsk</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="924" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg/180px-Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg/270px-Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg/360px-Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_the_Qianlong_Emperor_in_Court_Dress.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qianlong Emperor</a></div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of <a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qianlong Emperor</a>\'s long reign, the Qing Empire was at its zenith. China ruled more than <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires#All_empires_at_their_greatest_extent" title="List of largest empires">one-third of the world\'s population</a>, and had the largest economy in the world. By area it was <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires#All_empires_at_their_greatest_extent" title="List of largest empires">one of the largest empires ever</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1545" data-file-width="1063" decoding="async" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg/180px-Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg/270px-Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg/360px-Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Li_Hung_Chang_in_1896.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Li_Hongzhang" title="Li Hongzhang">Li Hongzhang</a>, a Chinese politician, general and diplomat of the late Qing dynasty.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 19th century the empire was internally stagnant and externally threatened by western powers. The defeat by the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a> (1840) led to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">Treaty of Nanking</a> (1842), under which <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hong_Kong_(1800s%E2%80%931930s)" title="History of Hong Kong (1800s&#8211;1930s)">Hong Kong</a> was ceded to Britain and importation of <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> (produced by British Empire territories) was allowed. Subsequent military defeats and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unequal_treaties" title="Unequal treaties">unequal treaties</a> with other western powers continued even after the fall of the Qing dynasty.\n</p><p>Internally the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping Rebellion</a> (1851&#8211;1864), a quasi-Christian religious movement led by the "Heavenly King" <a href="/wiki/Hong_Xiuquan" title="Hong Xiuquan">Hong Xiuquan</a>, raided roughly a third of Chinese territory for over a decade until they were finally crushed in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Nanking" title="Third Battle of Nanking">Third Battle of Nanking</a> in 1864. This was one of the largest wars in the 19th century in terms of troop involvement; there was massive loss of life, with <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_and_anthropogenic_disasters_by_death_toll#Wars_and_armed_conflicts" title="List of wars and anthropogenic disasters by death toll">a death toll of about 20 million</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> A string of civil disturbances followed, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punti%E2%80%93Hakka_Clan_Wars" title="Punti&#8211;Hakka Clan Wars">Punti&#8211;Hakka Clan Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nian_Rebellion" title="Nian Rebellion">Nian Rebellion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dungan_revolt_(1862%E2%80%931877)" title="Dungan revolt (1862&#8211;1877)">Dungan Revolt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Panthay_Rebellion" title="Panthay Rebellion">Panthay Rebellion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> All rebellions were ultimately put down, but at enormous cost and with millions dead, seriously weakening the central imperial authority. The <a href="/wiki/Eight_Banners" title="Eight Banners">Banner system</a> that the Manchus had relied upon for so long failed: Banner forces were unable to suppress the rebels, and the government called upon local officials in the provinces, who raised "New Armies", which successfully crushed the challenges to Qing authority. China never rebuilt a strong central army, and many local officials became warlords who used military power to effectively rule independently in their provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In response to calamities within the empire and threats from imperialism, the <a href="/wiki/Self-Strengthening_Movement" title="Self-Strengthening Movement">Self-Strengthening Movement</a> was an institutional reform in the second half of the 1800s. The aim was to modernize the empire, with prime emphasis on strengthening the military. However, the reform was undermined by corrupt officials, cynicism, and quarrels within the imperial family. As a result, the "<a href="/wiki/Beiyang_Fleet" title="Beiyang Fleet">Beiyang Fleet</a>" were soundly defeated in the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a> (1894&#8211;1895). The <a href="/wiki/Guangxu_Emperor" title="Guangxu Emperor">Guangxu Emperor</a> and the reformists then launched a more comprehensive reform effort, the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days%27_Reform" title="Hundred Days\' Reform">Hundred Days\' Reform</a> (1898), but it was soon overturned by the conservatives under <a href="/wiki/Empress_Dowager_Cixi" title="Empress Dowager Cixi">Empress Dowager Cixi</a> in a military coup.\n</p><p>At the turn of the 20th century, the violent <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxer Rebellion</a> opposed foreign influence in Northern China, and attacked Chinese Christians and missionaries. When Boxers entered Beijing, the Qing government ordered all foreigners to leave. But instead the foreigners and many Chinese were <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_the_International_Legations" title="Siege of the International Legations">besieged in the foreign legations quarter</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Eight-Nation_Alliance" title="Eight-Nation Alliance">Eight-Nation Alliance</a> sent the <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Expedition" title="Seymour Expedition">Seymour Expedition</a> of Japanese, Russian, Italian, German, French, American, and Austrian troops to relieve the siege. The Expedition was stopped by the Boxers at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Langfang" title="Battle of Langfang">Battle of Langfang</a> and forced to retreat. Due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dagu_Forts_(1900)" title="Battle of Dagu Forts (1900)">the Alliance\'s attack on the Dagu Forts</a>, the Qing government in response sided with the Boxers and declared war on the Alliance. There was <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tientsin" title="Battle of Tientsin">fierce fighting at Tientsin</a>. The Alliance formed the second, much larger <a href="/wiki/Gaselee_Expedition" title="Gaselee Expedition">Gaselee Expedition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Peking_(1900)" title="Battle of Peking (1900)">finally reached Beijing</a>; the Qing government evacuated to <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi\'an">Xi\'an</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Protocol" title="Boxer Protocol">Boxer Protocol</a> ended the war.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_China">Modern China</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Republic_of_China_.28since_1912.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China_(since_1912)">Republic of China (since 1912)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="History of the Republic of China">History of the Republic of China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912&#8211;1949)">Republic of China (1912&#8211;1949)</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Taiwan" title="History of Taiwan">History of Taiwan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="639" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/220px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/330px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/440px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Road" title="Nanjing Road">Nanjing Road</a> during <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a>, 1911.</div></div></div>\n<p>Frustrated by the Qing court\'s resistance to reform and by China\'s weakness, young officials, military officers, and students began to advocate the overthrow of the Qing dynasty and the creation of a republic. They were inspired by the revolutionary ideas of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>. A revolutionary military uprising, the <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_Uprising" title="Wuchang Uprising">Wuchang Uprising</a>, began on 10 October 1911, in <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_Republic_of_China_(1912)" title="Provisional Government of the Republic of China (1912)">provisional government of the Republic of China</a> was formed in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> on 12 March 1912. The <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> ended 2,000 years of dynastic rule in China.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:303px;max-width:303px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunyatsen1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1462" data-file-width="1059" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sunyatsen1.jpg/150px-Sunyatsen1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sunyatsen1.jpg/225px-Sunyatsen1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sunyatsen1.jpg/300px-Sunyatsen1.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> and the first provisional president of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912&#8211;49)">Republic of China</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuan_Shikai2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="349" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yuan_Shikai2.jpg/145px-Yuan_Shikai2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yuan_Shikai2.jpg/218px-Yuan_Shikai2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Yuan_Shikai2.jpg/290px-Yuan_Shikai2.jpg 2x" width="145"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>, the first president of the Republic of China.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>After the success of the overthrow of the Qing dynasty, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> was declared <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President</a>, but Sun was forced to turn power over to <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>, who commanded the <a href="/wiki/New_Army" title="New Army">New Army</a> and was Prime Minister under the Qing government, as part of the agreement to let the <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">last Qing monarch</a> abdicate (a decision Sun would later regret). Over the next few years, Yuan proceeded to abolish the national and provincial assemblies, and declared himself emperor in late 1915. Yuan\'s imperial ambitions were fiercely opposed by his subordinates; faced with the prospect of rebellion, he abdicated in March 1916, and died in June of that year.\n</p><p>Yuan\'s death in 1916 left a power vacuum in China; the republican government was all but shattered. This ushered in the <a href="/wiki/Warlord_Era" title="Warlord Era">Warlord Era</a>, during which much of the country was ruled by shifting coalitions of competing provincial military leaders.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="485" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/220px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/330px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/440px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Beijing college students rallied during the <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a>, dissatisfied with Article 156 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> for China (<a href="/wiki/Shandong_Problem" title="Shandong Problem">Shandong Problem</a>).</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1919, the <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> began as a response to the terms imposed on China by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> ending <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, but quickly became a nationwide protest movement about the domestic situation in China. The protests were a moral success as the cabinet fell and China refused to sign the Treaty of Versailles, which had awarded German holdings to Japan. The <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">New Culture Movement</a> stimulated by the May Fourth Movement waxed strong throughout the 1920s and 1930s. According to Ebrey:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>"Nationalism, patriotism, progress, science, democracy, and freedom were the goals; imperialism, feudalism, warlordism, autocracy, patriarchy, and blind adherence to tradition were the enemies. Intellectuals struggled with how to be strong and modern and yet Chinese, how to preserve China as a political entity in the world of competing nations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg"><img alt="Blue Sky White Sun Wholly Red Earth" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The flag of the Republic of China from 1928 to now.</div></div></div></dd></dl>\n<p>The discrediting of liberal Western philosophy amongst leftist Chinese intellectuals led to more radical lines of thought inspired by the Russian Revolution, and supported by agents of the Comintern sent to China by Moscow. This created the seeds for the irreconcilable conflict between the left and right in China that would dominate Chinese history for the rest of the century.\n</p><p>In the 1920s, Sun Yat-sen established a revolutionary base in south China, and set out to unite the fragmented nation. With assistance from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (itself fresh from Lenin\'s takeover), he entered into an alliance with the fledgling <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a>. After Sun\'s death from cancer in 1925, one of his prot&#233;g&#233;s, <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, seized control of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a></i> (Nationalist Party or KMT) and succeeded in bringing most of south and central China under its rule in a military campaign known as the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a> (1926&#8211;1927). Having defeated the warlords in south and central China by military force, Chiang was able to secure the nominal allegiance of the warlords in the North. In 1927, Chiang turned on the CPC and relentlessly chased the CPC armies and its leaders from their bases in southern and eastern China. In 1934, driven from their mountain bases such as the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Soviet_Republic" title="Chinese Soviet Republic">Chinese Soviet Republic</a>, the CPC forces embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Long_March" title="Long March">Long March</a> across China\'s most desolate terrain to the northwest, where they established a guerrilla base at <a href="/wiki/Yan%27an" title="Yan\'an">Yan\'an</a> in Shaanxi Province. During the Long March, the communists reorganized under a new leader, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> (Mao Tse-tung).\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (<a href="/wiki/Asiatic-Pacific_Theater" title="Asiatic-Pacific Theater">Asiatic-Pacific Theater</a>)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:136px;max-width:136px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:97px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="365" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg/134px-Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg/201px-Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg/268px-Japanese_bomber_over_Chungking.jpg 2x" width="134"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Chongqing" title="Bombing of Chongqing">Bombing of Chongqing</a> in 1940</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:97px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taierzhuang.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="391" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Taierzhuang.jpg/150px-Taierzhuang.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Taierzhuang.jpg/225px-Taierzhuang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Taierzhuang.jpg/300px-Taierzhuang.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Chinese soldiers in house-to-house fighting in the Battle of Tai\'erzhuang</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:143px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="955" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg/180px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg/270px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg/360px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_in_Battle_of_Shanghai_1937.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The Imperial Japanese Navy (IJN) Special Naval Landing Forces troops in gas masks prepare for an advance in the rubble of Shanghai, China.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:106px;max-width:106px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:143px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="242" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg/104px-Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg/156px-Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg/208px-Jiangjieshi-declare.jpg 2x" width="104"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek announced the Kuomintang policy of resistance against Japan at Lushan on July 10, 1937, three days after the <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_Incident" title="Marco Polo Bridge Incident">Seventy-seven Incident</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The bitter struggle between the KMT and the CPC continued, openly or clandestinely, through the 14-year-long Japanese occupation of various parts of the country (1931&#8211;1945). The two Chinese parties nominally formed a united front to oppose the Japanese in 1937, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937&#8211;1945), which became a part of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Japanese forces committed numerous <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">war atrocities</a> against the civilian population, including biological warfare (see <a href="/wiki/Unit_731" title="Unit 731">Unit 731</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Three_Alls_Policy" title="Three Alls Policy">Three Alls Policy</a> (<i>Sank&#333; Sakusen</i>), the three alls being: <i>"Kill All, Burn All and Loot All"</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the defeat of Japan in 1945, the war between the Nationalist government forces and the CPC resumed, after failed attempts at reconciliation and a negotiated settlement. By 1949, the CPC had established control over most of the country <i>(see <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>)</i>. Westad says the Communists won the Civil War because they made fewer military mistakes than Chiang, and because in his search for a powerful centralized government, Chiang antagonized too many interest groups in China. Furthermore, his party was weakened in the war against the Japanese. Meanwhile, the Communists told different groups, such as peasants, exactly what they wanted to hear, and cloaked themselves in the cover of Chinese Nationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> During the civil war both the Nationalists and Communists carried out mass atrocities, with millions of non-combatants killed by both sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> These included deaths from forced conscription and massacres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> When the Nationalist government forces were defeated by CPC forces in mainland China in 1949, the Nationalist government retreated to <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> with its forces, along with Chiang and most of the KMT leadership and a large number of their supporters; the Nationalist government had taken effective control of Taiwan at the end of WWII as part of the overall Japanese surrender, when Japanese troops in Taiwan surrendered to Republic of China troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="People.27s_Republic_of_China_.28since_1949.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="People\'s_Republic_of_China_(since_1949)">People\'s Republic of China (since 1949)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="History of the People\'s Republic of China">History of the People\'s Republic of China</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="613" data-file-width="780" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg/220px-PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg/330px-PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg/440px-PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PLA_Enters_Peking.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">People\'s Liberation Army</a> enters Beijing in the <a href="/wiki/Pingjin_Campaign" title="Pingjin Campaign">Pingjin Campaign</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Major combat in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> ended in 1949 with <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) pulling out of the mainland, with the government relocating to <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a> and maintaining control only over a few islands. The <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> was left in control of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>. On 1 October 1949, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> proclaimed the People\'s Republic of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_c_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_c-65">[65]</a></sup> "Communist China" and "Red China" were two common names for the PRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_d_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_d-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="414" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg/220px-Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg/330px-Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chairman <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> proclaiming the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People\'s Republic of China</a> in 1949.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg/220px-China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg/330px-China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg/440px-China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:China_10th_Anniversary_Parade_in_Beijing_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People\'s Republic of China 10th Anniversary Parade in Beijing</div></div></div>\n<p>The PRC was shaped by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_campaigns_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="List of campaigns of the Communist Party of China">series of campaigns</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five-year_plans_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Five-year plans of the People\'s Republic of China">five-year plans</a>. The economic and social plan known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> caused an estimated 45&#160;million deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akbar2010_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Akbar2010-67">[67]</a></sup> Mao\'s government carried out mass executions of landowners, instituted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivisation" title="Collectivisation">collectivisation</a> and implemented the <a href="/wiki/Laogai" title="Laogai">Laogai</a> camp system. Execution, deaths from forced labor and other atrocities resulted in millions of deaths under Mao. In 1966 Mao and his allies launched the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>, which continued until Mao\'s death a decade later. The Cultural Revolution, motivated by power struggles within the Party and a fear of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, led to a major upheaval in Chinese society.\n</p><p>In 1972, at the peak of the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a>, Mao and <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a> met US president <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> in Beijing to establish relations with the United States. In the same year, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758">PRC was admitted to the United Nations</a> in place of the Republic of China, with permanent membership of the Security Council.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg"><img alt="Blue Sky White Sun Wholly Red Earth" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The flag of the People\'s Republic of China since 1949.</div></div></div>\n<p>A power struggle followed Mao\'s death in 1976. The <a href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four" title="Gang of Four">Gang of Four</a> were arrested and blamed for the excesses of the Cultural Revolution, marking the end of a turbulent political era in China. <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> outmaneuvered Mao\'s anointed successor chairman <a href="/wiki/Hua_Guofeng" title="Hua Guofeng">Hua Guofeng</a>, and gradually emerged as the <i>de facto</i> leader over the next few years.\n</p><p>Deng Xiaoping was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paramount_Leader" title="Paramount Leader">Paramount Leader</a> of China from 1978 to 1992, although he never became the head of the party or state, and his influence within the Party led the country to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">significant economic reforms</a>. The Communist Party subsequently loosened governmental control over citizens\' personal lives and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_commune" title="People\'s commune">communes</a> were disbanded with many peasants receiving multiple land leases, which greatly increased incentives and agricultural production. In addition, there were many free market areas opened. The most successful free market areas was shenzhen. It is located in guangdong and the property tax free area still exists today. This turn of events marked China\'s transition from a planned economy to a mixed economy with an increasingly open market environment, a system termed by some<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_e_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_e-68">[68]</a></sup> as "<a href="/wiki/Market_socialism" title="Market socialism">market socialism</a>", and officially by the Communist Party of China as "<a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_Chinese_characteristics" title="Socialism with Chinese characteristics">Socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>". The PRC adopted its current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the People\'s Republic of China">constitution</a> on 4 December 1982.\n</p><p>In 1989 the death of former general secretary <a href="/wiki/Hu_Yaobang" title="Hu Yaobang">Hu Yaobang</a> helped to spark the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square_protests_of_1989" title="Tiananmen Square protests of 1989">Tiananmen Square protests</a> of that year, during which students and others campaigned for several months, speaking out against corruption and in favour of greater political reform, including democratic rights and freedom of speech. However, they were eventually put down on 4 June when <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">PLA</a> troops and vehicles entered and forcibly cleared the square, with many fatalities. This event was widely reported, and brought worldwide condemnation and sanctions against the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_f_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_f-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_g_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_g-70">[70]</a></sup> A filmed incident involving the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank_man" title="Tank man">tank man</a>" was seen worldwide.\n</p><p>CPC general secretary and PRC President <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Zemin" title="Jiang Zemin">Jiang Zemin</a> and PRC Premier <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Rongji" title="Zhu Rongji">Zhu Rongji</a>, both former mayors of Shanghai, led post-Tiananmen PRC in the 1990s. Under Jiang and Zhu\'s ten years of administration, the PRC\'s economic performance pulled an estimated 150&#160;million peasants out of poverty and sustained an average annual gross domestic product growth rate of 11.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_h_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_h-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_i_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_i-72">[72]</a></sup> The country formally joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 2001.\n</p><p>Although the PRC needs economic growth to spur its development, the government began to worry that rapid economic growth was degrading the country\'s resources and environment. Another concern is that certain sectors of society are not sufficiently benefiting from the PRC\'s economic development; one example of this is the wide gap between urban and rural areas. As a result, under former CPC general secretary and President <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> and Premier <a href="/wiki/Wen_Jiabao" title="Wen Jiabao">Wen Jiabao</a>, the PRC initiated policies to address issues of equitable distribution of resources, but the outcome was not known as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_China&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_j_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_j-73">[73]</a></sup> More than 40&#160;million farmers were displaced from their land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_k_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_k-74">[74]</a></sup> usually for economic development, contributing to 87,000 demonstrations and riots across China in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_l_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_l-75">[75]</a></sup> For much of the PRC\'s population, living standards improved very substantially and freedom increased, but political controls remained tight and rural areas poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation"
